Introduction and Front Matter

Introduction to Nur al-Idah and Its Author
Editor's preface praising the book and author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scope and authoritative status of Nur al-Idah within the Hanafi school and explain the role of its author, al-Shurunbulali.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah is a concise, relied-upon Hanafi matn covering ibadat, authored by the prominent later jurist al-Shurunbulali.

The editor's preface to Nur al-Idah introduces the book as a celebrated summary of Hanafi fiqh focusing on worship. It highlights that the text presents preponderant rulings without detailed proofs, and that the author, Hasan al-Shurunbulali, was a leading Azhari scholar. This lesson will help you understand why Nur al-Idah is a key text for Hanafi fiqh and who its author was.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's scope
Read the preface to determine which topics Nur al-Idah covers. It explicitly mentions the five categories of worship: taharah, salah, sawm, zakat, and hajj. Note that it does not cover other fiqh chapters such as muamalat or family law.
This is a focused matn on ibadat only.
2
Understand the book's method
The editor says the book presents rulings in clear, concise language without quoting evidences or detailed intra-madhhab disagreements. In cases of ikhtilaf, the author chooses the preponderant view (rajih) and sometimes notes the existence of disagreement in tarjih.
This makes Nur al-Idah a practical reference for fatwa.
3
Recognize the author's stature
The author is Hasan ibn 'Ammar al-Shurunbulali al-Misri (994-1069 AH), described as a foremost Hanafi jurist and a leading scholar at al-Azhar. His works are considered authoritative among later Hanafis.
Al-Shurunbulali is a muta'akhkhir (later) scholar, but his texts are widely relied upon.
4
Appreciate the book's position in Hanafi literature
The preface states that Nur al-Idah is 'one of the famous and relied-upon summaries among later scholars' and 'the relied-upon for fatwa'. This indicates its high rank in the Hanafi madhhab hierarchy of texts.
This explains why students of Hanafi fiqh often study it first for ibadat.

الطهارة والصلاة والصيام والزكاة والحج دون بقية الأبواب الفقهية. وفيه خلاصة الأحكام وزُبدتُها بعبارة واضحة موجزة سهلة، من غير ذكر لأدلتها ووجه استنباطها، وبدون بيان للخلاف بین أئمة المذهب أبي حنيفة وأصحابه إلا في مواضع يسيرة، بل يختار المؤلِّفُ حال الخلاف القول الراجح الذي جزم بصحته أهل الترجيح ويعتمده، وفي مسائل أخرى معدودة يشير إلى وجود خلاف في الترجيح فيها بين فقهاء الحنفية. هذا الكتاب من تأليف عمدة المحققين، وأحسن المتأخرين ملكةً في الفقه الحنفي، العلامة الشهير الشيخ حسن بن عمار الشرنبلالي المصري، المولود سنة ٩٩٤هـ ، والمتوفى بالقاهرة سنة ١٠٦٩هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
كان
من أعيان الفقهاء في زمانه وأعلام العلماء في أوانه، صاحب التأليفات النفيسة الحسنة الفائقة، والتحريرات الدقيقة الرائقة، مصباح الأزهر العالي، وكوكبه المنير المتلالي هذا مع خُلُقٍ حَسَن، وفصاحة
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Introduction of the Investigator. Praise be to Allah, and peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah, and upon his family and companions and those who follow him. To proceed: Indeed, the book 'Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah' is one of the famous and relied-upon summaries among later scholars in Hanafi fiqh. It is a solid and authoritative text, a great treasure to be stored, relied upon for fatwa, and it is foremost and best. This summary contains most of the legal rulings related to acts of worship, from purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and pilgrimage, excluding the remaining chapters of fiqh. It includes the essence and cream of the rulings in clear, concise, and easy wording, without mentioning their evidences and method of derivation, and without explaining the disagreement among the imams of the school – Abu Hanifa and his companions – except in a few places. Rather, in case of disagreement, the author chooses the preponderant opinion that the experts of tarjih have decisively deemed correct and relies upon it. In a few other issues, he indicates the existence of a disagreement in tarjih among Hanafi jurists. This book is authored by the pillar of investigators, the one with the best faculty among later scholars in Hanafi fiqh, the renowned scholar Sheikh Hasan ibn 'Ammar al-Shurunbulali al-Misri, born in 994 AH and died in Cairo in 1069 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He was one of the foremost jurists of his time and a leading scholar of his era, the author of precious, excellent, and superior works, and precise, elegant analyses. He was the lamp of the lofty al-Azhar and its radiant shining star, along with good character and eloquence.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This is the editor's (muhaqqiq) introduction to the book Nur al-Idah. He begins by praising Allah and invoking blessings on the Prophet. He then describes the book as a widely accepted concise text in Hanafi fiqh, focusing on the five pillars of worship: purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and pilgrimage. The book presents rulings without detailed proofs or inter-madhhab disputes, except where necessary, and in cases of disagreement within the Hanafi school, the author selects the preponderant view. The author is identified as the prominent Hanafi jurist Hasan al-Shurunbulali (d. 1069 AH), who was a leading scholar of his time, particularly associated with al-Azhar. The introduction sets the stage for the matn that follows, emphasizing its authority and practicality.

Key Terms
نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح (Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah): The title of the book meaning 'The Light of Clarification and the Salvation of Souls'.
الشرنبلالي (al-Shurunbulali): The nisbah of the author, referring to Shurnbulala in Egypt.
المتأخرين (al-muta'akhkhirin): Later scholars, as opposed to the early Hanafi masters like Abu Hanifa and his students.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preface, how does Nur al-Idah handle cases of disagreement among Hanafi imams?
A) It presents all opinions equally without preference.
B) It chooses the preponderant opinion (rajih) and sometimes notes disagreement in tarjih.
C) It avoids any mention of disagreement entirely.
D) It follows the view of Abu Hanifa only.

Key Takeaway
Nur al-Idah is a concise, authoritative Hanafi matn on ibadat, authored by the later scholar al-Shurunbulali, and it selects the preponderant view for fatwa.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Nur al-Idah: A Relied-Upon Hanafi Primer on Worship
Editor introduces the book's significance and scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Nur al-Idah is a relied-upon text in Hanafi fiqh and identify its scope and approach to legal disagreement.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah is a concise, authoritative primer covering Hanafi rulings on the five pillars, used for fatwa and teaching.

Before diving into fiqh rulings, it is important to understand the nature of the text we are studying. This lesson introduces one of the most widely used Hanafi summaries, Nur al-Idah. You will learn what kind of book it is, what it covers, and why scholars rely on it for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's subject matter
Read the editor's statement that the book includes 'most of the fiqh rulings related to acts of worship' (taharah, salah, sawm, zakat, hajj). Note that it does not cover other fiqh chapters.
This makes it a specialized text on ibadat.
2
Recognize the author and his status
The author is Hasan al-Shurunbulali (d. 1069 AH), a leading Hanafi scholar. The editor calls him 'the pillar of investigators' and 'the best of the later ones in mastery of Hanafi fiqh.'
His authority adds weight to the text's reliance.
3
Understand the text's style: mukhtasar
A mukhtasar presents rulings concisely without evidence or detailed disagreements. Nur al-Idah is a matn (text) meant for memorization and teaching.
The editor notes it omits evidence and most internal madhhab differences.
4
Note the role of tarjih
When disagreements exist, the author selects the preponderant opinion (rajih) that the scholars of tarjih have affirmed. In a few places, he signals ongoing tarjih disputes.
This makes the text a reliable source for the mufta bihi (operative opinion).
5
Assess the book's acceptance
The editor emphasizes that the book received wide acceptance, is used as a curriculum, and is relied upon for fatwa. This confirms its authority in the later Hanafi tradition.
Always verify the reliance status of a text before using it for fatwa.

مقدمة المحقق
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مقدمة المحقق
الحمد لله، والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد رسول الله، وعلى آله وصحبه ومن والاه، وبعد:
فإن كتاب: نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح» أحد المختصرات الشهيرة المعتمدة عند المتأخرين في الفقه الحنفي، وهو متن متين معتبر، وكنز عظيم يُدخر، عليه المعوّل في الفتوى، وهو المقدم والأولى. يضم هذا المختصر غالب الأحكام الفقهية المتعلقة بالعبادات، من الطهارة والصلاة والصيام والزكاة والحج دون بقية الأبواب الفقهية. وفيه خلاصة الأحكام وزُبدتُها بعبارة واضحة موجزة سهلة، من غير ذكر لأدلتها ووجه استنباطها، وبدون بيان للخلاف بين أئمة المذهب أبي حنيفة وأصحابه إلا في مواضع يسيرة، بل يختار المؤلِّفُ حال الخلاف القول الراجح الذي جزم بصحته أهل الترجيح ويعتمده، وفي مسائل أخرى معدودة يشير إلى وجود خلاف في الترجيح فيها بين فقهاء الحنفية. هذا الكتاب من تأليف عمدة المحققين، وأحسن المتأخرين ملكةً في الفقه الحنفي، العلامة الشهير الشيخ حسن بن عمار الشرنبلالي المصري، المولود سنة ٩٩٤هـ، والمتوفى بالقاهرة سنة ١٠٦٩هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
كان من أعيان الفقهاء في زمانه وأعلام العلماء في أوانه، صاحب التأليفات النفيسة الحسنة الفائقة، والتحريرات الدقيقة الرائقة، مصباح الأزهر العالي، وكوكبه المنير المتلالي هذا مع خُلُقٍ حَسَن، وفصاحة ولسن، ودين متين، وصلاح مبين.
ولقد كتب الله تعالى لهذا الكتاب : نور الإيضاح» قبولاً حسناً، ورزق رضاً كبيراً مستحسناً، وتداوله العلماء وطلابهم حتى تبوا في مجالسهم المكان الأسمى، ونال منهم قُرْباً وأنساً، وصار في غالب البلاد لطالبي الفقه الحنفي منهجاً ودرساً، وعُدَّةً وعُمدة ورأساً.
وهكذا قدر الله تعالى لهذا الكتاب هذا مع الإكرام والاحتفاء والإيثار أنه لم يُطبع إلى الآن طبعةً مفردةً صافية وافية، ولم يُحقق على نسخ خطية معتمدة، مع تعدد طبعاته.
نفسه، وقد أكرمني الله تعالى بتحقيق نصه وتحريره وتصحيحه وضبطه على عشر نسخ خطية من أقدم النسخ تاريخاً، وأجودها نصاً وتصحيحاً، إضافةً إلى ثلاث نسخ خطية أخرى من مراقي الفلاح شرح نور الإيضاح للمؤلف مع تفقير نصه، وإبراز معالم مسائله، وترتيبها وترقيمها. كما وضعت عليه تعليقات ضرورية يقتضيها النص، لا تُخرِج الكتاب قصد عن مؤلفه، وذلك من الناحية الفقهية لإيضاح ما لا بد منه، وكذلك من ناحية بيان الخلاف بين علماء المذهب إن كان قوياً حال عدم ذكر المؤلف له؛ وذلك للإشارة إلى وجوده، ولتحرير المعتمد في المذهب، مع لفتات لطيفة، ونكات علمية ظريفة، منسوبة لقائليها ومدوّنيها. وقد جاءت هذه التعليقات نتيجةَ ما دَعَتْ حاجة قارئ نصه إليه، وتأكدت رغبة دارسيه الوقوف عليه، مما لَمَسْتُه خلال تدريسي للكتاب مرات عدة، ولمستويات من الطلاب مختلفة متنوعة، بتكرر استفهامات من مبتغيها، واستفسارات علمية من محتاجيها.
وقد قدمت ذلك كله بترجمة لطيفة لمؤلف الكتاب، مع الاهتمام بذكر
Editor's Introduction
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful
Editor's Introduction
All praise is due to Allah, and blessings and peace be upon our master Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah, and upon his family and companions and those who follow him. To proceed:
Indeed, the book 'Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah' is one of the famous and relied-upon summaries of the later scholars in Hanafi fiqh. It is a solid and esteemed text, a great treasure to be preserved; reliance in fatwa is placed upon it, and it is the foremost and primary. This summary includes most of the fiqh rulings related to acts of worship, from purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and Hajj, without the remaining chapters of fiqh. In it is the essence of rulings and their cream, in a clear, concise, and easy expression, without mentioning their evidence and the manner of their derivation, and without explaining the disagreement among the imams of the madhhab—Abu Hanifa and his companions—except in a few places. Rather, in case of disagreement, the author chooses the preponderant opinion that the scholars of tarjih have decisively affirmed and upon which they rely. In a few other issues, he indicates the existence of disagreement in tarjih among Hanafi jurists. This book is authored by the pillar of investigators, the best of the later ones in mastery of Hanafi fiqh, the famous scholar Sheikh Hasan bin Ammar al-Shurunbulali al-Misri, born in 994 AH and died in Cairo in 1069 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He was among the leading jurists of his time and the flags of scholars of his era, possessing valuable, excellent, and superior writings, precise and elegant treatises—the lamp of the high Azhar and its shining star. He also had good character, eloquence, a strong tongue, firm religion, and apparent righteousness.
Allah the Exalted gave this book, 'Nur al-Idah', good acceptance and granted it great and approved pleasure. Scholars and their students circulated it until it attained the highest place in their gatherings, and they gained closeness and intimacy with it. It became, in most lands, for seekers of Hanafi fiqh a curriculum and lesson, a means and a foundation, and a head.
Thus Allah the Exalted decreed for this book, despite the honor and esteem and preference, that it had not yet been printed in a single, pure, and complete edition, nor had it been critically edited from reliable manuscript copies, despite its multiple prints. He himself enabled me to scrutinize its text, edit it, correct it, and vocalize it according to ten manuscript copies—the oldest in date and the best in text and correctness—in addition to three other manuscript copies of Maraqi al-Falah, the commentary on Nur al-Idah by the author, with referencing of its text, highlighting the outlines of its issues, and arranging and numbering them. I also placed upon it necessary annotations required by the text, not taking the book away from its author's intention. These annotations are from a fiqh standpoint to clarify what is indispensable, and also from the standpoint of explaining disagreement among scholars of the madhhab if it was strong while the author did not mention it; this is to indicate its existence and to edit the relied-upon position in the madhhab, along with subtle pointers and witty scientific notes attributed to their sayings and compilers. These annotations resulted from the need of the text's reader for them, and the confirmed desire of its students to know them—something I experienced during my teaching of the book several times to various levels of students, with repeated queries from those seeking them and scientific inquiries from those in need of them.
I have prefaced all that with a nice biography of the author of the book, with attention to mentioning
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is an editor's introduction to the book Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah. The editor, Dr. Saeed Bakdash, begins with the basmala and praise, then explains the significance of the book: it is a concise Hanafi fiqh text focusing on worship (taharah, salah, sawm, zakat, hajj). The author is Sheikh Hasan al-Shurunbulali (994-1069 AH), a prominent Egyptian Hanafi scholar. The text presents rulings without detailed evidence or extensive intra-madhhab disagreements, often selecting the preferred opinion (rajih). The editor then describes his methodology: he relied on ten manuscript copies plus three copies of the commentary Maraqi al-Falah by the same author. He added necessary annotations, especially explaining disagreements not mentioned by the author, and provided a biography of the author. The editor's work aims to produce a reliable critical edition that serves students and scholars.

Key Terms
مختصر (mukhtasar): A concise summary of fiqh rulings, omitting evidence and detailed differences.
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant opinion in a disagreement, chosen by experts for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main subject area of the book Nur al-Idah?
A) All areas of Hanafi fiqh including transactions and family law
B) Only the rulings related to acts of worship (ibadat)
C) A combination of fiqh and usul al-fiqh
D) Primarily judicial matters (qada) and evidence

Key Takeaway
Nur al-Idah is a concise yet authoritative Hanafi primer on ibadat, carefully selecting the preponderant opinion and serving as a reliable reference for fatwa.

The Art of Tahqiq: How a Critical Edition Preserves Hanafi Heritage
Editor describes his methodology for kritik edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the steps of tahqiq (critical editing) as practiced by Dr. Saeed Bakdash in his edition of Nur al-Idah and explain why such work is essential for reliable study.

Core Idea
Tahqiq uses multiple manuscripts and scholarly annotations to produce a text faithful to the author while clarifying relied-upon positions.

When studying a classical text, we rely on the work of editors who compare manuscripts and add helpful notes. This lesson explores the meticulous tahqiq methodology used in the edition of Nur al-Idah. Understanding this process helps you appreciate the reliability of the text and avoid common pitfalls in using critical editions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the need for tahqiq
The editor notes that despite many prints, Nur al-Idah had never been critically edited from manuscripts. This means previous editions may contain errors or be incomplete.
Tahqiq ensures the text matches what the author actually wrote.
2
List the manuscript sources used
The editor used ten manuscript copies of Nur al-Idah (oldest and best) plus three copies of the author's own commentary Maraqi al-Falah.
Multiple manuscripts allow collation to identify the most reliable reading.
3
Describe the editorial actions
The editor 'realized its text, edited it, corrected it, and vocalized it' (tahqiq, tahrir, tashih, dhabt). He also arranged and numbered issues.
Vocalization (dhabt) is crucial for Arabic texts to avoid misreading.
4
Understand the annotations
The editor added necessary annotations from a fiqh standpoint, clarifying what is indispensable. Where the author omitted a strong ikhtilaf, he explains it to show the relied-upon opinion.
These annotations are clearly distinguished from the original text.
5
Appreciate the pedagogical motive
The annotations were motivated by repeated questions from students during the editor's teaching. This makes the edition tailored to learners' needs.
A good edition bridges the gap between the matn and the student's understanding.

مقدمة المحقق
الحمد لله، والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد رسول الله، وعلى آله وصحبه ومن والاه، وبعد:
فإن كتاب: نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح» أحد المختصرات الشهيرة المعتمدة عند المتأخرين في الفقه الحنفي، وهو متن متين معتبر، وكنز عظيم يُدخر، عليه المعوّل في الفتوى، وهو المقدم والأولى. يضم هذا المختصر غالب الأحكام الفقهية المتعلقة بالعبادات، من الطهارة والصلاة والصيام والزكاة والحج دون بقية الأبواب الفقهية. وفيه خلاصة الأحكام وزُبدتُها بعبارة واضحة موجزة سهلة، من غير ذكر لأدلتها ووجه استنباطها، وبدون بيان للخلاف بين أئمة المذهب أبي حنيفة وأصحابه إلا في مواضع يسيرة، بل يختار المؤلِّفُ حال الخلاف القول الراجح الذي جزم بصحته أهل الترجيح ويعتمده، وفي مسائل أخرى معدودة يشير إلى وجود خلاف في الترجيح فيها بين فقهاء الحنفية. هذا الكتاب من تأليف عمدة المحققين، وأحسن المتأخرين ملكةً في الفقه الحنفي، العلامة الشهير الشيخ حسن بن عمار الشرنبلالي المصري، المولود سنة ٩٩٤هـ، والمتوفى بالقاهرة سنة ١٠٦٩هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
كان من أعيان الفقهاء في زمانه وأعلام العلماء في أوانه، صاحب التأليفات النفيسة الحسنة الفائقة، والتحريرات الدقيقة الرائقة، مصباح الأزهر العالي، وكوكبه المنير المتلالي هذا مع خُلُقٍ حَسَن، وفصاحة ولسن، ودين متين، وصلاح مبين.
ولقد كتب الله تعالى لهذا الكتاب : نور الإيضاح» قبولاً حسناً، ورزق رضاً كبيراً مستحسناً، وتداوله العلماء وطلابهم حتى تبوا في مجالسهم المكان الأسمى، ونال منهم قُرْباً وأنساً، وصار في غالب البلاد لطالبي الفقه الحنفي منهجاً ودرساً، وعُدَّةً وعُمدة ورأساً.
وهكذا قدر الله تعالى لهذا الكتاب هذا مع الإكرام والاحتفاء والإيثار أنه لم يُطبع إلى الآن طبعةً مفردةً صافية وافية، ولم يُحقق على نسخ خطية معتمدة، مع تعدد طبعاته.
نفسه، وقد أكرمني الله تعالى بتحقيق نصه وتحريره وتصحيحه وضبطه على عشر نسخ خطية من أقدم النسخ تاريخاً، وأجودها نصاً وتصحيحاً، إضافةً إلى ثلاث نسخ خطية أخرى من مراقي الفلاح شرح نور الإيضاح للمؤلف مع تفقير نصه، وإبراز معالم مسائله، وترتيبها وترقيمها. كما وضعت عليه تعليقات ضرورية يقتضيها النص، لا تُخرِج الكتاب قصد عن مؤلفه، وذلك من الناحية الفقهية لإيضاح ما لا بد منه، وكذلك من ناحية بيان الخلاف بين علماء المذهب إن كان قوياً حال عدم ذكر المؤلف له؛ وذلك للإشارة إلى وجوده، ولتحرير المعتمد في المذهب، مع لفتات لطيفة، ونكات علمية ظريفة، منسوبة لقائليها ومدوّنيها. وقد جاءت هذه التعليقات نتيجةَ ما دَعَتْ حاجة قارئ نصه إليه، وتأكدت رغبة دارسيه الوقوف عليه، مما لَمَسْتُه خلال تدريسي للكتاب مرات عدة، ولمستويات من الطلاب مختلفة متنوعة، بتكرر استفهامات من مبتغيها، واستفسارات علمية من محتاجيها.
وقد قدمت ذلك كله بترجمة لطيفة لمؤلف الكتاب، مع الاهتمام بذكر
Editor's Introduction
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful
Editor's Introduction
All praise is due to Allah, and blessings and peace be upon our master Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah, and upon his family and companions and those who follow him. To proceed:
Indeed, the book 'Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah' is one of the famous and relied-upon summaries of the later scholars in Hanafi fiqh. It is a solid and esteemed text, a great treasure to be preserved; reliance in fatwa is placed upon it, and it is the foremost and primary. This summary includes most of the fiqh rulings related to acts of worship, from purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and Hajj, without the remaining chapters of fiqh. In it is the essence of rulings and their cream, in a clear, concise, and easy expression, without mentioning their evidence and the manner of their derivation, and without explaining the disagreement among the imams of the madhhab—Abu Hanifa and his companions—except in a few places. Rather, in case of disagreement, the author chooses the preponderant opinion that the scholars of tarjih have decisively affirmed and upon which they rely. In a few other issues, he indicates the existence of disagreement in tarjih among Hanafi jurists. This book is authored by the pillar of investigators, the best of the later ones in mastery of Hanafi fiqh, the famous scholar Sheikh Hasan bin Ammar al-Shurunbulali al-Misri, born in 994 AH and died in Cairo in 1069 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He was among the leading jurists of his time and the flags of scholars of his era, possessing valuable, excellent, and superior writings, precise and elegant treatises—the lamp of the high Azhar and its shining star. He also had good character, eloquence, a strong tongue, firm religion, and apparent righteousness.
Allah the Exalted gave this book, 'Nur al-Idah', good acceptance and granted it great and approved pleasure. Scholars and their students circulated it until it attained the highest place in their gatherings, and they gained closeness and intimacy with it. It became, in most lands, for seekers of Hanafi fiqh a curriculum and lesson, a means and a foundation, and a head.
Thus Allah the Exalted decreed for this book, despite the honor and esteem and preference, that it had not yet been printed in a single, pure, and complete edition, nor had it been critically edited from reliable manuscript copies, despite its multiple prints. He himself enabled me to scrutinize its text, edit it, correct it, and vocalize it according to ten manuscript copies—the oldest in date and the best in text and correctness—in addition to three other manuscript copies of Maraqi al-Falah, the commentary on Nur al-Idah by the author, with referencing of its text, highlighting the outlines of its issues, and arranging and numbering them. I also placed upon it necessary annotations required by the text, not taking the book away from its author's intention. These annotations are from a fiqh standpoint to clarify what is indispensable, and also from the standpoint of explaining disagreement among scholars of the madhhab if it was strong while the author did not mention it; this is to indicate its existence and to edit the relied-upon position in the madhhab, along with subtle pointers and witty scientific notes attributed to their sayings and compilers. These annotations resulted from the need of the text's reader for them, and the confirmed desire of its students to know them—something I experienced during my teaching of the book several times to various levels of students, with repeated queries from those seeking them and scientific inquiries from those in need of them.
I have prefaced all that with a nice biography of the author of the book, with attention to mentioning
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is an editor's introduction to the book Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah. The editor, Dr. Saeed Bakdash, begins with the basmala and praise, then explains the significance of the book: it is a concise Hanafi fiqh text focusing on worship (taharah, salah, sawm, zakat, hajj). The author is Sheikh Hasan al-Shurunbulali (994-1069 AH), a prominent Egyptian Hanafi scholar. The text presents rulings without detailed evidence or extensive intra-madhhab disagreements, often selecting the preferred opinion (rajih). The editor then describes his methodology: he relied on ten manuscript copies plus three copies of the commentary Maraqi al-Falah by the same author. He added necessary annotations, especially explaining disagreements not mentioned by the author, and provided a biography of the author. The editor's work aims to produce a reliable critical edition that serves students and scholars.

Key Terms
التحقيق (al-tahqiq): Critical editing based on multiple manuscripts to establish a reliable text.
الضبط (al-dhabt): Vocalization of the Arabic text to ensure correct reading.
التعليقات (al-ta'liqat): Annotations added by the editor to clarify or supplement the text.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Critical Edition: A Scholar's Toolkit for Hanafi Texts
Editorial methodology for a critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the key features of a critical edition of a Hanafi fiqh text and identify the editorial steps described in the introduction.

Core Idea
A critical edition ensures the text is as close as possible to the author's original, using multiple manuscripts and scholarly care.

This lesson introduces the methodological framework behind the critical edition of 'Nur al-Idah' you are about to study. Understanding the editor's work helps you appreciate the reliability of the text and the scholarly tradition it represents.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Need for Critical Editions
Consider why a widely used book like Nur al-Idah might still not have a proper critical edition. What problems arise from relying on uncorrected prints?
Think about scribal errors, missing text, and variations between copies.
2
Identify the Editor's Sources
The editor used ten manuscripts of the main text and three copies of its commentary. Note the importance of using multiple, old, and well-corrected copies.
3
Recognize the Editor's Additions
The editor added footnotes to clarify fiqh points and indicate strong disagreements within the Hanafi school that the author did not mention. This helps you navigate the text's legal content.
These additions are marked and do not distort the original.
4
Appreciate the Editor's Goals
The editor aimed to present the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the school, along with necessary clarifications, without changing the author's intent.

... and a pure tongue, a firm religion, and manifest righteousness.
And Allah the Exalted has destined for this book, 'Nur al-Idah', a good acceptance, and granted it great and praiseworthy satisfaction. Scholars and their students have circulated it until they have attained the highest place in their gatherings, and they have gained closeness and familiarity with it. It has become a curriculum and a lesson for students of Hanafi fiqh in most lands, and a tool, a mainstay, and a pillar.

And Allah the Exalted has honored me by editing its text, revising, correcting, and dotting it based on ten manuscript copies of the oldest dates and the best text and correction, in addition to three other manuscript copies of 'Maraqi al-Falah', the commentary on 'Nur al-Idah' by the author, along with referencing its text, highlighting the features of its issues, and arranging and numbering them. Commentary
This is the editor's introduction to the critical edition of Nur al-Idah. The editor, Dr. Sa'id Bakdash, explains that despite the book's widespread acceptance and use among Hanafi students, it had never been published in a proper critical edition. He describes his methodology: he relied on ten manuscript copies of the text itself and additionally used three copies of the commentary 'Maraqi al-Falah' by the same author. He added necessary footnotes to clarify juristic points and to indicate when there are strong differences of opinion within the Hanafi school that the original author did not mention. The goal is to present the relied-upon position in the school. He also includes a biography of the author. The editor concludes with prayers and hopes for acceptance of his work.

Key Terms
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical edition — the scholarly process of editing a text using manuscript sources to produce a reliable version.
نسخة خطية (nuskha khattiyya): Manuscript copy — a hand-written copy of a book, used as a source in critical editing.
مذهب (madhhab): School of law — here referring to the Hanafi school, whose internal disagreements the editor notes.

Introduction and Front Matter

Structure and Commentaries of Nur al-Idah
Front matter describing the book's composition and commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the composition of Nur al-Idah, identify its two main commentaries, and explain their relationship and scope.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah is a foundational Hanafi matn with two layered commentaries: detailed Imdad al-Fattah and abridged Maraqi al-Falah.

Nur al-Idah by al-Shurunbulali is a concise text on Hanafi fiqh that became a standard reference. This lesson unpacks its history: what topics it originally covered, how the author later expanded it, and the two commentaries he wrote. Understanding this structure helps you place the matn within the broader Hanafi teaching tradition and choose the right commentary for your study level.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and original scope
Read the first line: the author initially wrote on taharah, salah, and sawm in 1032 AH. Note that zakat and hajj were added later.
Original core: purification, prayer, fasting only.
2
Trace the commentaries
Two commentaries: Imdad al-Fattah (larger, 360 pages, completed 1046 AH) and Maraqi al-Falah (abridgment, 145 pages, written 7.5 years later). Maraqi al-Falah is a summary of Imdad al-Fattah.
Imdad = detailed; Maraqi = abridged.
3
Note the later supplementation
After 1054 AH, the author added rulings on zakat and hajj briefly. These were appended to Maraqi al-Falah in manuscripts. The author did not comment on them; al-Tahtawi later covered all chapters in his gloss.
Supplement not commented by author.
4
Understand the proportion of topics
Two-thirds of the book covers salah (including special prayers), one-third covers sawm, zakat, and hajj. Zakat is the briefest section.
Salah dominates; zakat is brief.
5
Interpret the title
The author explains: 'Nur al-Idah' means 'The Light of Clarification' – knowledge is light and salvation. This underscores the intended role of the book as an illuminating guide.
Title reflects purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب نور الإيضاح ومكانته
كتب المؤلف رحمه الله أولاً في نور الإيضاح أحكام الطهارة والصلاة والصيام، وذلك سنة ١٠٣٢هـ، ثم شرحه شرحين، سمى الأول منهما وهو ورقة، الأكبر: «إمداد الفتاح، وعدد أوراقه كما قال المؤلف ٣٦٠ وانتهى منه سنة ١٠٤٦هـ، وسمى الثاني وهو مختصر من الأول: «مراقي الفلاح»، وعدد أوراقه ١٤٥ ورقة.
وكانت المدة بين الشرحين نحواً من سبع سنوات ونصف، كما قال الطحطاوي، ثم أتم بعد ذلك، أي بعد سنة ١٠٥٤هـ، أحكام الزكاة والحج باختصار، وألحقت في النسخ الخطية بمراقي الفلاح.
وينبه إلى أن المؤلف لم يشرح التتمة، في حين أن الطحطاوي في حاشيته على مراقي الفلاح أتم تحشيته على الأبواب كلها. وقد أخذت أحكام الصلاة من الكتاب قدر الثلثين، وهذا مع أحكام بقية الصلوات الخاصة كالجمعة والعيدين والاستسقاء وغيرها، وشمل الثلث الباقي من الكتاب أحكام الصوم والزكاة والحج، وكان أخصرها كتاب الزكاة.
ومما يُظهر أهمية الكتاب عنوانه الناطق عن مضمونه، وقد قال عنه المؤلف في مستهل شرحه إمداد الفتاح وسميته: «نور الإيضاح»، إذ العلم نور ، ونجاة الأرواح»، إذ لا نجاة إلا بالعلم. اهـ.
The book Nur al-Idah and its status. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) first wrote in Nur al-Idah the rulings of taharah, salah, and siyam, in the year 1032 AH. Then he wrote two commentaries on it; he named the first of them, and it is... leaves, the larger: 'Imdad al-Fattah', and its number of leaves as the author said 360, and he finished it in 1046 AH. And he named the second, which is an abridgment of the first: 'Maraqi al-Falah', and its number of leaves is 145 leaves. The period between the two commentaries was about seven and a half years, as al-Tahtawi said. Then after that, i.e. after 1054 AH, he completed the rulings of zakat and hajj briefly, and they were appended in the manuscript copies to Maraqi al-Falah. It is noted that the author did not commentate on the supplement, whereas al-Tahtawi in his gloss on Maraqi al-Falah completed his gloss on all chapters. The rulings of salah occupy about two-thirds of the book, and this includes the rulings of special prayers like Jumu'ah, the two Eids, istisqa', etc. The remaining one-third of the book includes the rulings of sawm, zakat, and hajj, and the briefest of these is the book of zakat. Among the things that show the importance of the book is its title, which speaks of its content. The author said about it at the beginning of his commentary Imdad al-Fattah: 'I named it Nur al-Idah, for knowledge is light and salvation of souls, for there is no salvation except through knowledge.' End.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This is an introduction to the book Nur al-Idah by al-Shurunbulali. It explains that the author initially wrote only on purification, prayer and fasting in 1032 AH. Later he wrote two commentaries: the larger 'Imdad al-Fattah' (360 pages, completed 1046 AH) and the abridged 'Maraqi al-Falah' (145 pages). After 1054 AH he added sections on zakat and hajj, which were appended to Maraqi al-Falah. Notably, the author did not write a commentary on the added sections, but al-Tahtawi later covered them in his gloss (hashiya) on Maraqi al-Falah. The text also notes the proportion of the book: two-thirds on salah (including Jumu'ah, Eid, rain prayer), and one-third on fasting, zakat, and hajj, with zakat being the briefest. The passage concludes by quoting the author's explanation of the title: 'Nur al-Idah' meaning the light of clarification, as knowledge is light and salvation.

Key Terms
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): The title of the book, meaning 'The Light of Clarification', referring to the illumination it provides in fiqh.
إمداد الفتاح (Imdad al-Fattah): The larger commentary on Nur al-Idah, meaning 'Supply of the Opener'.
مراقي الفلاح (Maraqi al-Falah): The abridged commentary on Nur al-Idah, meaning 'Ascents of Success'.
الطحطاوي (al-Tahtawi): The scholar who wrote a gloss (hashiya) on Maraqi al-Falah covering all chapters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which part of Nur al-Idah is the briefest?
A) Salah
B) Sawm
C) Zakat
D) Hajj

Key Takeaway
Nur al-Idah is a compact Hanafi matn with a two-tier commentary system, later expanded to cover all pillars, making it a foundational text in the school.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Introduction: The Book Nur al-Idah and Its Place
Introduction of the Hanafi fiqh text Nur al-Idah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scope and significance of the Hanafi fiqh text Nur al-Idah and its major commentaries.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah is a foundational yet concise Hanafi fiqh text that later scholars relied upon and extensively commented.

This passage introduces the book Nur al-Idah, a core matn in the Hanafi school. Written initially covering purification, prayer, and fasting, the author later added sections on zakat and hajj. The significance of this text is highlighted by the fact that the author himself wrote two commentaries on it, and numerous later scholars produced glosses, demonstrating its central place in Hanafi legal education and practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's composition timeline and original scope.
Note that the author first wrote the matn covering purification, prayer, and fasting in 1032 AH, and later appended zakat and hajj after 1054 AH. This shows the gradual development of the text.
The matn originally did not cover zakat and hajj; they were added later and appended to manuscripts.
2
Recognize the author's own commentaries and their sizes.
The author wrote two commentaries: the larger 'Imdad al-Fattah' (360 folios) and the abridgment 'Maraqi al-Falah' (145 folios). Understand the relationship between them: the second is a summary of the first.
The time gap between the two commentaries was about seven and a half years.
3
Understand the book's authority by noting its citation by major Hanafi authorities.
Later authorities like the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Ibn Abidin frequently quote Nur al-Idah with approval. The multitude of commentaries and glosses further attest to its importance.
Imam al-Laknawi described it as 'a solid text in fiqh'.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب نور الإيضاح ومكانته
كتب المؤلف رحمه الله أولاً في نور الإيضاح أحكام الطهارة والصلاة والصيام، وذلك سنة ١٠٣٢هـ، ثم شرحه شرحين، سمى الأول منهما وهو الأكبر: «إمداد الفتاح، وعدد أوراقه كما قال المؤلف ٣٦٠ وانتهى منه سنة ١٠٤٦هـ، وسمى الثاني وهو مختصر من الأول: «مراقي الفلاح»، وعدد أوراقه ١٤٥ ورقة. وكانت المدة بين الشرحين نحواً من سبع سنوات ونصف، كما قال الطحطاوي، ثم أتم بعد ذلك، أي بعد سنة ١٠٥٤هـ، أحكام الزكاة والحج باختصار، وألحقت في النسخ الخطية بمراقي الفلاح. وينبه إلى أن المؤلف لم يشرح التتمة، في حين أن الطحطاوي في حاشيته على مراقي الفلاح أتم تحشيته على الأبواب كلها. وقد أخذت أحكام الصلاة من الكتاب قدر الثلثين، وهذا مع أحكام بقية الصلوات الخاصة كالجمعة والعيدين والاستسقاء وغيرها، وشمل الثلث الباقي من الكتاب أحكام الصوم والزكاة والحج، وكان أخصرها كتاب الزكاة.
ومما يُظهر أهمية الكتاب عنوانه الناطق عن مضمونه، وقد قال عنه المؤلف في مستهل شرحه إمداد الفتاح وسميته: «نور الإيضاح»، إذ العلم نور ، ونجاة الأرواح»، إذ لا نجاة إلا بالعلم. اهـ.
وعن مكانة نور الإيضاح يقول الإمام اللكنوي (ت ١٣٠٤هـ)(١): وقد طالعتُ من تصنيفاته نور الإيضاح: متن متين في الفقه». اهـ ويدل على مكانة هذا الكتاب وأهميته عند الحنفية: اعتماده عند كبار متأخري الحنفية وعمدتهم، كصاحب الدر المختار، ومحشيه ابن عابدين في رد المحتار، فقد أكثرا من النقل عنه مع إقراره، وكذلك عن شرحي المصنف له : مراقي الفلاح، وإمداد الفتاح.
ومما يُبرز المنزلة العالية لهذا الكتاب عند علماء المذهب: كثرة الشروح والحواشي عليه وعلى شروحه (۲)، ومن أهمها: شرحي المؤلف نفسه : إمداد الفتاح، ومراقي الفلاح، وكذلك الحاشية النفيسة للطحطاوي ت ١٢٣١هـ) على المراقي.
وللعلامة محمد علاء الدين (ت (١٣٠٦هـ) ابن الإمام ابن عابدين شرح على نور الإيضاح، لكنه لم يتم سماه: معراج الفلاح شرح نور الإيضاح، وَصَلَ فيه إلى باب الإمامة أي إلى منتصف الكتاب تقريباً، وهو شرح كبير يقع في (۱۷۸) ورقة ، منه نسخة بخط المؤلف في المكتبة الظاهرية بدمشق، برقم (٦٦٦٧).
ومن الحواشي المفيدة جداً في حل عبارات الكتاب: حاشية الشيخ محمد إعزاز علي المرادآبادي الأمروهوي الديوبندي (ت١٣٧٤هـ)، (۱) التعليقات السنية على الفوائد البهية ص ٥٨. (۲) وقد استقصاها الأخ الشيخ محمد طلحة في مقدمته لحاشية محمد إعزاز على نور الإيضاح ص ۸۹.
Book of Nur al-Idah and its Place. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) first wrote in Nur al-Idah the rulings of purification, prayer, and fasting in the year 1032 AH. Then he explained it with two commentaries: the first, which is the larger, he named 'Imdad al-Fattah', and its number of folios, as the author said, is 360, and he completed it in 1046 AH. The second, which is an abridgment of the first, he named 'Maraqi al-Falah', and its number of folios is 145. The period between the two commentaries was about seven and a half years, as al-Tahtawi said. Then after that, i.e., after 1054 AH, he completed the rulings of zakat and hajj briefly, and they were appended in the manuscript copies to 'Maraqi al-Falah'. He notes that the author did not explain the supplement, while al-Tahtawi in his gloss on 'Maraqi al-Falah' completed his gloss on all the chapters. The rulings of prayer take up about two-thirds of the book, along with rulings of special prayers like Friday, the two Eids, rain prayer, etc., and the remaining third includes the rulings of fasting, zakat, and hajj, with the book on zakat being the briefest. Among what shows the importance of the book is its title, which speaks of its content. The author said about it at the beginning of his commentary 'Imdad al-Fattah': 'I named it Nur al-Idah (The Light of Clarification), for knowledge is light, and salvation of souls, for there is no salvation except through knowledge.' As for the place of Nur al-Idah, Imam al-Laknawi (d. 1304 AH) said: 'I have examined among his writings Nur al-Idah: a solid text in fiqh.' This indicates the status and importance of this book among the Hanafis: its reliance by the senior later Hanafis and their main authorities, like the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its annotator Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar, for they frequently quoted from it with approval, and likewise from the author's two commentaries on it: Maraqi al-Falah and Imdad al-Fattah. Among what highlights the high rank of this book among scholars of the madhhab is the multitude of commentaries and glosses on it and on its commentaries. Among the most important are the author's own two commentaries: Imdad al-Fattah and Maraqi al-Falah, and the valuable gloss of al-Tahtawi (d. 1231 AH) on al-Maraqi. And the scholar Muhammad Ala al-Din (d. 1306 AH), son of Imam Ibn Abidin, wrote a commentary on Nur al-Idah but did not complete it; he named it 'Miraj al-Falah: Commentary on Nur al-Idah', and he reached the chapter on Imamate, about halfway through the book. It is a large commentary comprising 178 folios, with a manuscript copy in the author's hand in the Zahiriyya library in Damascus, number 6667. Among the very useful glosses in explaining the expressions of the book is the gloss of Shaykh Muhammad Izzaz Ali al-Muradabadi al-Amrohawi al-Diyubandi (d. 1374 AH). (1) al-Taliqat al-Saniyya ala al-Fawaid al-Bahiyya, p. 58. (2) His brother Shaykh Muhammad Talha has enumerated them in his introduction to the gloss of Muhammad Izzaz on Nur al-Idah, p. 89.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the book Nur al-Idah and its place in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that the author initially wrote the book covering the rulings of purification (taharah), prayer (salah), and fasting (sawm) in 1032 AH. Later, he wrote two commentaries on his own book: a larger one called 'Imdad al-Fattah' (completed 1046 AH) and a shorter one abridged from it called 'Maraqi al-Falah' (145 folios). The time between the two commentaries was about seven and a half years. Subsequently, after 1054 AH, the author added concise sections on zakat and hajj, which were appended to manuscript copies of Maraqi al-Falah. The passage notes that the author did not write a commentary on these additions, but al-Tahtawi included them in his gloss on Maraqi al-Falah. The content of the book is roughly two-thirds prayer (including special prayers like Friday, Eid, and rain prayer) and one-third fasting, zakat, and hajj, with zakat being the most concise. The title 'Nur al-Idah' (Light of Clarification) is explained by the author: knowledge is light, and salvation is only through knowledge. The passage then cites Imam al-Laknawi's praise of the book as a solid text in fiqh. The book's importance is further evidenced by its frequent citation by later Hanafi authorities like the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar. Many commentaries and glosses were written on it, including the author's own, al-Tahtawi's gloss, a commentary by Muhammad Ala al-Din (Ibn Abidin's son) which reached the chapter on Imamate, and a gloss by Muhammad Izzaz Ali al-Muradabadi. This passage establishes the authoritative status of Nur al-Idah within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): The title of a foundational Hanafi fiqh text covering purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and hajj.
إمداد الفتاح (Imdad al-Fattah): The larger commentary on Nur al-Idah, written by the same author, completed in 1046 AH.
مراقي الفلاح (Maraqi al-Falah): An abridged commentary on Nur al-Idah, also by the same author, consisting of 145 folios.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Nur al-Idah is a concise yet comprehensive Hanafi fiqh primer, supported by extensive later scholarship.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Status and Commentaries of Nur al-Idah
Describing the significance, commentaries, and a note on controversial rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of Nur al-Idah in the Hanafi school and critically evaluate the claim that thirty of its rulings are unreliable.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah is a central Hanafi matn; the thirty contested rulings reflect normal tarjih differences, not errors.

This lesson introduces Nur al-Idah, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text by al-Shurunbalali. We will explore its high status among later authorities, the numerous commentaries written on it, and address a common misconception about thirty rulings that some claim are unreliable. Understanding this clarifies how tarjih works within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and its author
Locate the name of the book (Nur al-Idah) and its author (al-Shurunbalali) in the passage. Note the praise from Imam al-Lakhnawi that it is a 'solid text in fiqh'.
2
Recognize the evidence of its importance
Observe that later authorities like the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Ibn Abidin relied on it, and that many commentaries were written on it. List the major commentaries mentioned.
This shows the book's centrality in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the claim about thirty rulings
Read the 'Note' section. Some claim that about thirty rulings in Nur al-Idah are not reliable. Identify the basis of this claim.
The claim is about specific rulings where al-Shurunbalali took a certain position.
4
Analyze the author's rebuttal
The passage explains that these thirty issues are merely cases of differing tarjih within the school, not errors. Al-Shurunbalali adopted a preferred opinion that other Hanafis may disagree with, which is normal scholarly practice.
The author gives examples of other scholars having different tarjih in their own works.
5
Apply the concept of tarjih
Reflect on how tarjih works: multiple valid opinions exist, and a scholar chooses based on evidence. This is not weakness but a feature of fiqh methodology.
The key takeaway: ikhtilaf within the school does not invalidate a ruling.

كِتَابُ نُورِ الإِيضَاحِ وَمَكَانَتُهُ
وَعَنْ مَكَانَةِ نُورِ الإِيضَاحِ يَقُولُ الإِمَامُ اللَّكْنَوِيُّ (ت ١٣٠٤هـ)(١): وَقَدْ طَالَعْتُ مِنْ تَصْنِيفَاتِهِ نُورَ الإِيضَاحِ: مَتْنٌ مَتِينٌ فِي الْفِقْهِ". اهـ وَيَدُلُّ عَلَى مَكَانَةِ هَذَا الْكِتَابِ وَأَهَمِّيَّتِهِ عِنْدَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ: اعْتِمَادُهُ عِنْدَ كِبَارِ مُتَأَخِّرِي الْحَنَفِيَّةِ وَعُمْدَتِهِمْ، كَصَاحِبِ الدُّرِّ الْمُخْتَارِ، وَمُحَشِّيهِ ابْنِ عَابِدِينَ فِي رَدِّ الْمُحْتَارِ، فَقَدْ أَكْثَرَا مِنَ النَّقْلِ عَنْهُ مَعَ إِقْرَارِهِ، وَكَذَلِكَ عَنْ شَرْحَيْ الْمُصَنِّفِ لَهُ : مِرَاقِي الْفَلاَحِ، وَإِمْدَادِ الْفَتَّاحِ.
وَمِمَّا يُبْرِزُ الْمَنْزِلَةَ الْعَالِيَةَ لِهَذَا الْكِتَابِ عِنْدَ عُلَمَاءِ الْمَذْهَبِ: كَثْرَةُ الشُّرُوحِ وَالْحَوَاشِي عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى شُرُوحِهِ (۲)، وَمِنْ أَهَمِّهَا: شَرْحَا الْمُؤَلِّفِ نَفْسِهِ : إِمْدَادُ الْفَتَّاحِ، وَمِرَاقِي الْفَلاَحِ، وَكَذَلِكَ الْحَاشِيَةُ النَّفِيسَةُ لِلطَّحْطَاوِيِّ (ت ١٢٣١هـ) عَلَى الْمَرَاقِي.
وَلِلْعَلاَّمَةِ مُحَمَّدٍ عَلاءِ الدِّينِ (ت ١٣٠٦هـ) ابْنِ الإِمَامِ ابْنِ عَابِدِينَ شَرْحٍ عَلَى نُورِ الإِيضَاحِ، لَكِنَّهُ لَمْ يَتِمَّ سَمَّاهُ: مِعْرَاجَ الْفَلاَحِ شَرْحَ نُورِ الإِيضَاحِ، وَصَلَ فِيهِ إِلَى بَابِ الإِمَامَةِ أَيْ إِلَى مُنْتَصَفِ الْكِتَابِ تَقْرِيباً، وَهُوَ شَرْحٌ كَبِيرٌ يَقَعُ فِي (١٧٨) وَرَقَةً، مِنْهُ نُسْخَةٌ بِخَطِّ الْمُؤَلِّفِ فِي الْمَكْتَبَةِ الظَّاهِرِيَّةِ بِدِمَشْقَ، بِرَقْمِ (٦٦٦٧).
وَمِنَ الْحَوَاشِي الْمُفِيدَةِ جِدّاً فِي حَلِّ عِبَارَاتِ الْكِتَابِ: حَاشِيَةُ الشَّيْخِ مُحَمَّدٍ إِعْزَازِ عَلِيٍّ الْمُرَادَآبَادِيِّ الأَمْرُوهَوِيِّ الدِّيُوبَنْدِيِّ (ت١٣٧٤هـ)، وَاسْمُهَا: الإِصْبَاحُ عَلَى نُورِ الإِيضَاحِ، وَالَّتِي قَدَّمَ لَهَا الأَخُ الشَّيْخُ مُحَمَّدٌ طَلْحَةُ بِلاَلٍ بِمُقَدِّمَةٍ مُفِيدَةٍ مَطْوَلَةٍ، وَفِيهَا تَرْجَمَةٌ مُوَسَّعَةٌ لِلشُّرُنْبُلاَلِيِّ. وَهَكَذَا لِمَا تَقَدَّمَ كُلِّهِ وَلإِخْلاَصِ صَاحِبِهِ أَبِي الإِخْلاَصِ - وَاللهُ أَعْلَمُ - صَارَ نُورُ الإِيضَاحِ عُدَّةً لِلْمُبْتَدِي، وَعُمْدَةً لِلْمُنْتَهِي، وَمَرْجِعاً مُعْتَمَداً لِكُلِّ فَقِيهٍ حَنَفِيٍّ، بَلْ حَظِيَ أَنْ يَكُونَ مِنْ مَحْفُوظَاتِ كَثِيرٍ مِنَ الطَّلَبَةِ وَالْمُهْتَمِّينَ بِحِفْظِ الْمُتُونِ وَالْمُخْتَصَرَاتِ .
تَنْبِيهٌ :
وَأَمَّا مَا ذَكَرَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ مِنْ أَنَّ أَحْكَامَ الْعَلاَّمَةِ الشُّرُنْبُلاَلِيِّ فِي نُورِ الإِيضَاحِ صَحِيحَةٌ مُعْتَمَدَةٌ مَا عَدَا زُهَاءَ ثَلاَثِينَ مَسْأَلَةً، فَهَذَا الاسْتِثْنَاءُ فِي الثَّلاَثِينَ غَيْرُ صَحِيحٍ، وَبَيَانُ ذَلِكَ فِيمَا يَلِي:
هُنَاكَ مَسَائِلُ كَثِيرَةٌ فِي الْمَذْهَبِ اخْتُلِفَ فِيهَا الْقَوْلُ بَيْنَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ، وَاخْتُلِفَ التَّصْحِيحُ فِيهَا، وَهَذِهِ الْمَسَائِلُ الثَّلاَثُونَ الَّتِي ذَكَرُوهَا هِيَ مِنْ هَذَا الصِّنْفِ، وَقَدِ اعْتَمَدَ فِيهَا الشُّرُنْبُلاَلِيُّ تَرْجِيحاً مُعَيَّناً فِي الْمَذْهَبِ، خَالَفَهُ فِيهِ فَرِيقٌ آخَرُ مِنَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ، فَهُوَ اخْتِلاَفٌ فِي وِجْهَاتِ النَّظَرِ فِي التَّرْجِيحِ وَالاِعْتِمَادِ بَيْنَ عُلَمَاءِ الْمَذْهَبِ، لاَ أَنَّ حُكْمَهُ فِيهَا غَيْرُ صَحِيحٍ. بَلْ إِنَّ الشُّرُنْبُلاَلِيَّ نَفْسَهُ قَدْ يَخْتَلِفُ رَأْيُهُ فِي التَّرْجِيحِ فِي الْمَسْأَلَةِ نَفْسِهَا بَيْنَ نُورِ الإِيضَاحِ وَبَيْنَ شَرْحِهِ مِرَاقِي الْفَلاَحِ، وَهَذَا يَحْصُلُ كَثِيراً لِعُلَمَاءِ الْمَذْهَبِ، مِثْلَ الْمُوصِلِيِّ بَيْنَ الْمُخْتَارِ وَالاِخْتِيَارِ وَكَذَلِكَ النَّسَفِيِّ بَيْنَ كَنْزِ الْمَسَائِلِ وَ [؟] (١) وَهُمْ: دُكْتُورُ مُحَمَّدٌ عَبْدِ اللَّطِيفِ الْفَرْفُورِ فِي كِتَابِهِ: ابْنُ عَابِدِينَ وَأَثَرُهُ فِي الْفِقْهِ ٧٨٦/٢، مُتَابِعاً بِذَلِكَ الشَّيْخَ عَبْدَ الْجَلِيلِ الْعَطَا فِي تَحْقِيقِهِ لِنُورِ الإِيضَاحِ، وَتَابَعَهُمَا الأَخُ الشَّيْخُ مُحَمَّدٌ طَلْحَةُ بِلاَلٌ ص٧٩.
(١) التَّعْلِيقَاتُ السَّنِيَّةُ عَلَى الْفَوَائِدِ الْبَهِيَّةِ ص ٥٨.
(۲) وَقَدِ اسْتَقْصَاهَا الأَخُ الشَّيْخُ مُحَمَّدٌ طَلْحَةُ فِي مُقَدِّمَتِهِ لِحَاشِيَةِ مُحَمَّدٍ إِعْزَازِ عَلَى نُورِ الإِيضَاحِ ص ٨٩.
The Book of Nur al-Idah and Its Status

Regarding the status of Nur al-Idah, Imam al-Lakhnawi (d. 1304 AH) says: 'I have reviewed among his works Nur al-Idah: a solid text in fiqh.' This indicates the status and importance of this book among the Hanafis: its reliance by the later major Hanafis and their authorities, such as the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its commentator Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar, who frequently quote it with approval, and likewise the two commentaries of the author himself: Maraqi al-Falah and Imdad al-Fattah.

What further highlights the high status of this book among the scholars of the school is the abundance of commentaries and glosses on it and on its commentaries (2), the most important of which are the author's own two commentaries: Imdad al-Fattah and Maraqi al-Falah, as well as the valuable gloss by al-Tahtawi (d. 1231 AH) on al-Maraqi.

And the scholar Muhammad Ala' al-Din (d. 1306 AH), the son of Imam Ibn Abidin, has a commentary on Nur al-Idah, but he did not complete it; he named it Mi'raj al-Falah Sharh Nur al-Idah. He reached the chapter of Imamate, i.e., about half the book. It is a large commentary consisting of 178 folios; a copy in the author's handwriting exists in al-Zahiriyya Library in Damascus under number 6667.

Among the very useful glosses for explaining the book's expressions is the gloss of Shaykh Muhammad I'zaz 'Ali al-Muradabadi al-Amruhavi al-Diyubandi (d. 1374 AH), named al-Isbah 'ala Nur al-Idah, for which the brother Shaykh Muhammad Talha Bilal wrote a lengthy beneficial introduction, including an extensive biography of al-Shurunbalali. Thus, due to all the above and the sincerity of its author Abu al-Ikhlas—and Allah knows best—Nur al-Idah became the stock of the beginner, the mainstay of the advanced, and a reliable reference for every Hanafi jurist; indeed it became among the memorized texts of many students and those interested in memorizing texts and abridgments.

Note:

As for what some have mentioned that the rulings of al-Shurunbalali in Nur al-Idah are sound and reliable except for about thirty issues, this exception of thirty is not correct. The explanation is as follows:

There are many issues in the school regarding which there is difference of opinion among the Hanafis and difference in the preferred (tashih). These thirty issues that they mentioned are of this kind. In them, al-Shurunbalali adopted a specific tarjih within the school, which another group of Hanafis opposed. So it is a difference in perspectives of tarjih and reliance among the scholars of the school, not that his rulings are unsound. Indeed, al-Shurunbalali himself may differ in his tarjih opinion on the same issue between Nur al-Idah and his commentary Maraqi al-Falah, and this happens often among scholars of the school, such as al-Mawsili between al-Mukhtar and al-Ikhtiyar, and likewise al-Nasafi between Kanz al-Masa'il and [؟]. (1) And they are: Dr. Muhammad 'Abd al-Latif al-Farfur in his book Ibn Abidin wa Atharuhu fi al-Fiqh 2/786, following thereby Shaykh 'Abd al-Jalil al-'Ata in his edition of Nur al-Idah, and the brother Shaykh Muhammad Talha Bilal followed them, p. 79.

(1) Al-Ta'liqat al-Saniyya 'ala al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, p. 58.
(2) And the brother Shaykh Muhammad Talha has comprehensively covered them in his introduction to the gloss of Muhammad I'zaz on Nur al-Idah, p. 89.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the book Nur al-Idah and its status in the Hanafi school. It opens by quoting Imam al-Lakhnawi, who praises the work as a solid matn (text) in fiqh. The passage then highlights the book's importance by noting that later authoritative Hanafi scholars like Ibn Abidin frequently relied on it in their works. It also mentions the many commentaries and glosses written on it, indicating its central place in the curriculum. The author then lists several important commentaries: the author's own Maraqi al-Falah and Imdad al-Fattah, al-Tahtawi's gloss on Maraqi, and a commentary by Ibn Abidin's son. Finally, it addresses a note clarifying a misconception: some claim that about thirty rulings in Nur al-Idah are not reliable. The author explains that these are merely cases where al-Shurunbalali adopted one preferred opinion among varying views within the Hanafi school, and this does not render them unsound. He gives examples of other scholars whose tarjih (preference) differed between their own works, showing this is normal scholarly practice.

Key Terms
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): The book itself, a foundational Hanafi fiqh matn by al-Shurunbalali (Abu al-Ikhlas).
متن (matn): A concise text containing core rulings, typically memorized by students.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of weighing and preferring one juristic opinion over other valid opinions within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason some claim thirty rulings in Nur al-Idah are not reliable?
A) They are contrary to the Quran and Sunnah.
B) They are based on weak evidence.
C) They are cases where al-Shurunbalali adopted one tarjih among divergent views in the school.
D) They were all abandoned by later Hanafis.

Key Takeaway
Nur al-Idah is a core Hanafi text whose 'controversial' rulings are simply instances of normal tarjih differences, not errors.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

The Integrity of Nur al-Idah and Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Refuting claims that thirty rulings in Nur al-Idah are incorrect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the thirty allegedly incorrect rulings in Nur al-Idah are actually valid instances of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
Difference of opinion (ikhtilaf) among Hanafi scholars does not imply error; tarjih determines the operative view.

This lesson addresses a common criticism that Nur al-Idah contains about thirty incorrect rulings. The author of the passage defends the book, explaining that these rulings are cases of legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, where al-Shurunbulali adopted a particular tarjih. Understanding this helps appreciate the methodological richness of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Read the passage and note the specific claim being refuted: that thirty rulings in Nur al-Idah are incorrect.
The claim is that all of al-Shurunbulali's rulings are correct except about thirty.
2
Analyze the author's refutation
Examine how the author argues that these thirty are not errors but rather cases of ikhtilaf. He states that they are from among many issues where Hanafis differed, and al-Shurunbulali adopted a specific tarjih.
The author asserts that difference in tarjih does not make a ruling incorrect.
3
Connect to Hanafi methodology
Identify the key concepts: ikhtilaf (disagreement), tarjih (preference), and mufta bihi (operative opinion). Understand that multiple valid opinions exist within the madhhab.
Al-Shurunbulali's own differing tarjih between Nur al-Idah and Maraqi al-Falah illustrates this normal scholarly process.
4
Consider the broader context
Reflect on how this defense applies to other Hanafi texts like Kanz al-Daqa'iq and al-Mukhtar. The passage highlights that such differences are common and do not undermine a book's authority.
The mufta bihi may vary depending on the scholar's tarjih; this is a feature, not a flaw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب نور الإيضاح ومكانته
واسمها: الإصباح على نور الإيضاح، والتي قدم لها الأخ الشيخ محمد طلحة بلال بمقدمة مفيدة مطولة، وفيها ترجمة موسعة للشرنبلالي. وهكذا لما تقدم كله ولإخلاص صاحبه أبي الإخلاص - والله أعلم - صار نور الإيضاح عدة للمبتدي، وعمدة للمنتهي، ومرجعاً معتمداً لكل فقيه حنفي، بل حظي أن يكون من محفوظات كثير من الطلبة والمهتمين بحفظ المتون والمختصرات .
تنبيه :
(1) وأما ما ذكره بعضهم من أن أحكام العلامة الشرنبلالي في نور الإيضاح صحيحة معتمدة ماعدا زهاء ثلاثين مسألة، فهذا الاستثناء في الثلاثين غير صحيح، وبيان ذلك فيما يلي:
هناك مسائل كثيرة في المذهب اختلف فيها القول بين الحنفية، واختلف التصحيح فيها، وهذه المسائل الثلاثين التي ذكروها هي من هذا الصنف، وقد اعتمد فيها الشرنبلالي ترجيحاً معيناً في المذهب، خالفه فيه فريق آخر من الحنفية، فهو اختلاف في وجهات النظر في الترجيح والاعتماد بين علماء المذهب، لا أن حكمه فيها غير صحيح. بل إن الشرنبلالي نفسه قد يختلف رأيه في الترجيح في بين نور الإيضاح وبين شرحه مراقي الفلاح، وهذا يحصل كثيراً لعلماء المذهب، مثل الموصلي بين المختار والاختيار وكذلك النسفي بين كنز الدقائق والكافي شرح الوافي أصل الكنز، وهذا شيء معهود في كل المذاهب الفقهية.
ومسألة اختلاف علماء المذهب في المفتى به في مسائل المذهب، مسألة عريضة شائكةٌ تحتاج إلى تتبع كبير، وينظر لتصورها بشكل مختصر مجمل ما سجله العلامة قاسم في تصحيح القدوري» من خلاف علماء المذهب، وما كتبتُه في مقدمة تحقيقي لكتاب: كنز الدقائق للنسفي، وكتاب: المختار للفتوى للموصلي، في مسألة هل المقدم في الفتوى دائماً قول الإمام أم قول الصاحبين، أم قول أحدهما؟ واختلاف ضوابط الترجيح بين علماء المذهب في ذلك، والله أعلم.
Book of Nur al-Idah and its Status
And its name: al-Isbah 'ala Nur al-Idah, which was prefaced by the brother Shaykh Muhammad Talha Bilal with a lengthy beneficial introduction, containing an extensive biography of al-Shurunbulali. And thus, due to all that has preceded and due to the sincerity of its author Abu al-Ikhlas - and Allah knows best - Nur al-Idah became a provision for the beginner, a mainstay for the advanced, and a reliable reference for every Hanafi jurist; indeed it was fortunate to be among the memorized texts of many students and those interested in memorizing matn and abridged works.
Note:
(1) As for what some have mentioned, that the rulings of 'Allamah al-Shurunbulali in Nur al-Idah are correct and relied upon except for about thirty issues, this exception of thirty is incorrect. The explanation is as follows:
There are many issues in the madhhab regarding which there is disagreement among the Hanafis, and there is difference in tarjih (preference) among them. These thirty issues they mentioned are of this type. Al-Shurunbulali adopted a particular weighting (tarjih) within the madhhab, with which another group of Hanafis disagreed. So it is a difference in perspectives regarding weighting and reliance among the scholars of the madhhab, not that his ruling therein is incorrect. Rather, al-Shurunbulali himself may differ in his opinion on weighting between Nur al-Idah and his commentary Maraqi al-Falah. This happens frequently among scholars of the madhhab, such as al-Mawsili between al-Mukhtar and al-Ikhtiyar, and al-Nasafi between Kanz al-Daqa'iq and al-Kafi Sharh al-Wafi Asl al-Kanz. This is a common phenomenon in all schools of fiqh.
And the issue of the scholars of the madhhab differing regarding the mufta bihi (operative opinion) in the issues of the madhhab is a broad and thorny issue requiring extensive investigation. For a concise overview, one may refer to what 'Allamah Qasim recorded in his Tashih al-Quduri regarding the differences among the scholars of the madhhab, and what I wrote in the introduction to my editing of the book Kanz al-Daqa'iq by al-Nasafi and the book al-Mukhtar lil-Fatwa by al-Mawsili, on the question: Is the opinion of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) always given precedence in fatwa, or the opinion of the two companions, or the opinion of one of them? And the different criteria for weighting (tarjih) among the scholars of the madhhab in that regard. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is from the introduction to a modern edition of Nur al-Idah, discussing the book's status and defending it against criticism. The passage first states that Nur al-Idah has become an essential text for both beginners and advanced Hanafi jurists. It then addresses a claim that about thirty rulings in the book are incorrect. The author refutes this, explaining that these rulings are not incorrect but rather represent valid ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school. Al-Shurunbulali chose a particular tarjih (preferred view) in these matters, which other Hanafi scholars may have disagreed with, but this does not make his rulings wrong. The author points out that such differences in tarjih occur even within the works of a single scholar (like al-Shurunbulali himself) and among other Hanafi authorities like al-Mawsili and al-Nasafi. The passage concludes by noting that the issue of determining the mufta bihi (operative opinion for fatwa) in the Hanafi madhhab is complex and requires careful study, referencing works by 'Allamah Qasim and the author's own introductions to Kanz al-Daqa'iq and al-Mukhtar lil-Fatwa.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of preferring one scholarly opinion over another within the Hanafi madhhab.
مفتى به (mufta bihi): The operative opinion that is relied upon for issuing fatwas.
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): Disagreement among scholars on a legal ruling, often due to different interpretations or evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the claim that Nur al-Idah contains thirty incorrect rulings unfounded?
A) Al-Shurunbulali later corrected those rulings in his commentary Maraqi al-Falah.
B) Those thirty issues are cases of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, and al-Shurunbulali's rulings are valid preferred views.
C) The thirty issues are actually from another book, not Nur al-Idah.
D) The scholars who made the claim were not qualified to judge.

Key Takeaway
The thirty rulings in Nur al-Idah are not errors; they are valid Hanafi opinions based on tarjih, reflecting the rich tradition of ikhtilaf within the madhhab.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Concept of Mufta Bih and Tarjih in the Hanafi School
Introduction to book status and fiqh methodology nuances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school sometimes adopts a view other than Abu Hanifa's as mufta bih and identify the criteria for tarjih.

Core Idea
The mufta bih in Hanafi fiqh is not always the view of Abu Hanifa; later scholars may prefer the view of Abu Yusuf or Muhammad.

This lesson explores a foundational yet often misunderstood feature of Hanafi fiqh: the determination of the mufta bih—the operative opinion for fatwa. The passage from Nur al-Idah highlights that within the Hanafi school, there is a complex process of tarjih (preference) that may lead to adopting a view other than that of Abu Hanifa. Understanding this dynamic is essential for anyone using Hanafi texts, as the mufta bih can vary across time and context.

Guided Path
1
Identify key terms
Define 'mufta bih' and 'tarjih' from the passage. Note that mufta bih is the opinion relied upon for fatwa, and tarjih is the process of preferring one opinion over another.
These terms are central to understanding the flexibility within the Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the chain of commentaries
The passage mentions al-Daqaiq and al-Kafi as commentaries on al-Wafi, which is the source of al-Kanz. This shows that Nur al-Idah is part of a layered textual tradition common to all madhahib.
This chain indicates how later texts build upon earlier ones.
3
Analyze the issue of mufta bih
The passage states that the determination of mufta bih is a broad and intricate issue. Reflect on why it is complex: there are multiple authoritative imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and later scholars may differ in their preferences.
The complexity arises from different tarjih criteria and the evolution of the school.
4
Refer to cited sources
The author points to Allamah Qasim's Tashih al-Quduri and his own editions of Kanz al-Daqaiq and al-Mukhtar li al-Fatwa as resources for understanding these differences. Consider how these works address the issue.
These texts are key references for studying tarjih within the Hanafi school.
5
Consider practical implications
Understand that a mufti cannot simply assume the view of Abu Hanifa is always operative. He must be aware of the tarjih process and the mufta bih for each issue.
This knowledge prevents incorrect fatwas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب نور الإيضاح ومكانته الدقائق والكافي شرح الوافي أصل الكنز، وهذا شيء معهود في كل المذاهب الفقهية. ومسألة اختلاف علماء المذهب في المفتى به في مسائل المذهب، مسألة عريضة شائكةٌ تحتاج إلى تتبع كبير، وينظر لتصورها بشكل مختصر مجمل ما سجله العلامة قاسم في تصحيح القدوري» من خلاف علماء المذهب، وما كتبتُه في مقدمة تحقيقي لكتاب: كنز الدقائق للنسفي، وكتاب: المختار للفتوى للموصلي، في مسألة هل المقدم في الفتوى دائماً قول الإمام أم قول الصاحبين، أم قول أحدهما؟ واختلاف ضوابط الترجيح بين علماء المذهب في ذلك، والله أعلم.
The book Nur al-Idah and its status: al-Daqaiq and al-Kafi are commentaries on al-Wafi which is the source of al-Kanz, and this is customary in all jurisprudential schools. The issue of the disagreement of the scholars of the school regarding the mufta bih (the opinion given for fatwa) in the matters of the school is a broad and intricate issue that requires extensive investigation. To understand it briefly and summarily, one may look at what Allamah Qasim recorded in Tashih al-Quduri regarding the differences among the scholars of the school, and what I wrote in the introduction of my edition of Kanz al-Daqaiq by al-Nasafi and al-Mukhtar li al-Fatwa by al-Mawsili, on the issue: Is the preferred opinion for fatwa always the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) or the statement of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), or the statement of one of them? And the differences in the principles of tarjih (preference) among the scholars of the school in that regard. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is an introductory note about the book Nur al-Idah and its place in the Hanafi tradition. The author highlights that the work is part of a chain of commentaries: al-Daqaiq and al-Kafi are commentaries on al-Wafi, which itself is the source of al-Kanz. This layered structure is common across all legal schools. The passage then raises a key methodological issue in the Hanafi school: determining which opinion is 'mufta bih' (the operative one for issuing fatwas). This is a complex topic because there are differences among the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) and later scholars often differed on tarjih (preference). The author refers to two important works: Tashih al-Quduri by Allamah Qasim, and his own critical editions of Kanz al-Daqaiq and al-Mukhtar li al-Fatwa, which discuss whether the mufta bih is always the Imam's view or sometimes the companions' views. The passage sets the stage for understanding that Nur al-Idah, like other texts, operates within this contested tradition.

Key Terms
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The legal opinion that is deemed authoritative and relied upon for issuing fatwas within the Hanafi school.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of preferring one legal opinion over another based on established criteria (e.g., strength of evidence, consistency with principles).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main issue discussed regarding the Hanafi school?
A) The differences between al-Daqaiq and al-Kafi
B) The determination of the mufta bih opinion
C) The biography of Allamah Qasim
D) The definition of al-Wafi

Key Takeaway
The mufta bih in the Hanafi school is not static; it is determined through a process of tarjih that may favor the view of Abu Yusuf or Muhammad over Abu Hanifa.

The Author's Methodology in Nur al-Idah
Author's methodology from the introduction and editorial commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five key methodological features of Nur al-Idah and explain why the author relies on ahl al-tarjih.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah is a concise Hanafi fiqh primer on worship, using only rulings deemed sound by scholars of tarjih.

This lesson introduces the methodology of Hasan al-Shurunbulali in his classic work Nur al-Idah. Understanding a jurist's method is crucial for correctly interpreting and applying the rulings within. We will examine the author's own preface and the five key features that define this concise text on acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's preface in the source
Identify the author's stated purpose: to compile a concise work on 'ibadat for beginners, based on preferred opinions, avoiding verbosity.
The phrase 'without verbosity' (min ghayri itnab) signals the concise style.
2
Extract the scope of the book
From the passage, the book covers only the rulings of purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and hajj—the five pillars of worship.
It excludes other fiqh topics like transactions, marriage, etc.
3
Note the reliance on ahl al-tarjih
The author mentions only rulings that the 'people of tarjih' have deemed correct. This means the book presents the mufta bihi (operative) position without exploring weaker or minority views.
This is a pedagogical choice to avoid confusing beginners.
4
Identify omission of imam names
The author rarely names which Hanafi imam (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is behind a ruling. This simplifies the text but requires the reader to trust that the ruling is sound.
It encourages focus on the ruling itself rather than its historical attribution.
5
Summarize the five methodological points
List them: (1) limited to 'ibadat; (2) collects scattered issues; (3) concise sequential presentation; (4) rarely names imams; (5) only includes rulings deemed correct by ahl al-tarjih.
These five points define the texture and reliability of Nur al-Idah.

Source Text

منهج المؤلف في نور الإيضاح قال المؤلف رحمه الله في مقدمة نور الإيضاح إنه التمس مني بعض الأخلاء ـ عاملنا الله وإياهم بلطفه الخفي ـ أن أعمل ما تشتت مقدمة في العبادات تقرب على المبتدي المسائل في المطولات، فاستعنت بالله تعالى وأجبتُه ؛ طالباً للثواب، ولا أذكر إلا ما جزم بصحته أهلُ الترجيح، من غير إطناب». اهـ من خلال هذه المقدمة، ومما لمسته أثناء خدمتي للكتاب يمكن إبراز منهج المؤلف في النقاط التالية : ١- إن كتاب نور الإيضاح خاص بأحكام العبادات فقط، من الطهارة والصلاة والصوم والزكاة والحج دون بقية الأبواب الفقهية. ٢- جَمَعَ المؤلف في هذا الكتاب شتات المسائل الفقهية المتفرقة في الشروح والمطولات، ولم يصرح بها، وبذلك يسر على طلاب العلم وقوفهم عليها مجموعة في مكان واحد. من منهج المؤلف في نور الإيضاح أنه ذكر أحكام المسائل بشكل متسلسل، وبصورة موجزة مختصرة، دون تطويل وإطناب. ٤- لا يذكر المؤلف في المسائل اسم صاحب القول من أئمة المذهب، كالإمام أبي حنيفة والصاحبين إلا في مواضع يسيرة، كما لا يذكر أسماء المرجحين للقول الذي يختاره، إلا نادراً. ه لا يورد الشرنبلالي فيه من الأحكام إلا ما جزم بصحته أهلُ
The Author's Methodology in Nur al-Idah. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, said in the introduction of Nur al-Idah: 'Some close friends—may Allah treat us and them with His hidden kindness—asked me to compile a scattered introduction in the acts of worship that would bring closer to the beginner the issues found in lengthy works. So I sought help from Allah Almighty and responded to them, seeking reward, and I mention only what the people of tarjih have deemed correct, without verbosity.' End quote. From this introduction and what I have perceived during my service to the book, the author's methodology can be highlighted in the following points: 1- The book Nur al-Idah is specific to the rulings of acts of worship only, from purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and hajj, excluding the rest of the chapters of fiqh. 2- The author gathered in this book the scattered legal issues from the commentaries and lengthy works without explicitly citing them, thus making it easy for students of knowledge to find them collected in one place. 3- The author mentioned the rulings of issues in a sequential manner, in a brief and concise form, without prolongation and verbosity. 4- The author does not mention in the issues the name of the author of the statement among the imams of the school, such as Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions, except in a few places, nor does he mention the names of those who gave preference to the opinion he chooses, except rarely. 5- Al-Shurunbulali only includes in it rulings that the people of tarjih have deemed correct.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a methodological preface explaining the scope and style of Nur al-Idah. The author, Hasan al-Shurunbulali, explains that he wrote the book at the request of friends, aiming to create a concise text on 'ibadat (acts of worship) for beginners. He relies only on opinions that the scholars of tarjih (preference) have deemed sound. The commentary then extracts five key points: (1) the book covers only the five pillars of worship (taharah, salah, sawm, zakat, hajj); (2) it collects scattered rulings from longer works into one accessible volume; (3) the rulings are presented in a sequential, concise manner without unnecessary detail; (4) the author rarely names the specific imam (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) behind a ruling, nor does he mention the names of those who did the tarjih; (5) he only includes rulings that have been deemed correct by the people of tarjih. This methodology makes the book a reliable primer for students, though it omits the rich attribution and debate found in larger works. The approach reflects a pedagogical choice to focus on the operative law (mufta bih) rather than on the history of ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
أهل الترجيح (ahl al-tarjih): The scholars who have the authority to prefer one legal opinion over another within the Hanafi school.
إطناب (itnab): Verbose or lengthy exposition, which the author deliberately avoids to keep the book concise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is a key feature of the author's methodology in Nur al-Idah?
A) He includes all opinions of the Hanafi imams
B) He names the imams for every ruling
C) He only mentions rulings deemed correct by ahl al-tarjih
D) He provides lengthy discussions of evidence

Key Takeaway
Nur al-Idah is a concise primer on Hanafi worship rulings, relying solely on the mufta bihi positions of ahl al-tarjih, without imam names or extended discussion.
