Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Author's Methodology in Nur al-Idah
Describes the author's methodology in writing Nur al-Idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key methodological principles of al-Shurunbulali in writing Nur al-Idah and identify how he selects rulings using ahl al-tarjih.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah relies on ahl al-tarjih, not always the zahir al-riwayah.

This lesson introduces you to the methodology of Imam al-Shurunbulali in his concise Hanafi fiqh text, Nur al-Idah. Understanding his method is essential for correctly interpreting the rulings in the book. The author explains his criteria: he includes only what the 'people of tarjih' have definitively deemed correct, and sometimes prefers a weaker narration if it aligns with a hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated goal
He compiled a concise work on ibadat for beginners, gathering scattered rulings from longer works.
The goal is to make fiqh accessible to novices.
2
Understand the source of rulings
He relies on ahl al-tarjih, the later scholars who weigh evidence, not necessarily the earliest narrations.
This differs from earlier mutun that present zahir al-riwayah.
3
Recognize the scope
The book covers only ibadat: purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj.
Not a comprehensive fiqh manual.
4
Analyze the tarjih example
In the adhan of a person without wudu, he follows a weaker narration (Hasan ibn Ziyad) because it matches the hadith, even though the zahir al-riwayah is different.
Shows textual evidence can override transmission strength.
5
Note his treatment of ikhtilaf
When disagreement among tarjih scholars is strong, he sometimes mentions both sides without preferring one.
Example: sajdah al-tilawah obligation from hearing by a sleeping or insane person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منهج المؤلف في نور الإيضاح
قال المؤلف رحمه الله في مقدمة نور الإيضاح إنه التمس مني بعض الأخلاء ـ عاملنا الله وإياهم بلطفه الخفي ـ أن أجمع ما تشتت مقدمة في العبادات تقرب على المبتدي المسائل في المطولات، فاستعنت بالله تعالى وأجبتُه ; طالباً للثواب، ولا أذكر إلا ما جزم بصحته أهلُ الترجيح، من غير إطناب». اهـ من خلال هذه المقدمة، ومما لمسته أثناء خدمتي للكتاب يمكن إبراز منهج المؤلف في النقاط التالية :
١- إن كتاب نور الإيضاح خاص بأحكام العبادات فقط، من الطهارة والصلاة والصوم والزكاة والحج دون بقية الأبواب الفقهية.
٢- جَمَعَ المؤلف في هذا الكتاب شتات المسائل الفقهية المتفرقة في الشروح والمطولات، ولم يصرح بها، وبذلك يسر على طلاب العلم وقوفهم عليها مجموعة في مكان واحد.
من منهج المؤلف في نور الإيضاح أنه ذكر أحكام المسائل بشكل متسلسل، وبصورة موجزة مختصرة، دون تطويل وإطناب.
٤- لا يذكر المؤلف في المسائل اسم صاحب القول من أئمة المذهب، كالإمام أبي حنيفة والصاحبين إلا في مواضع يسيرة، كما لا يذكر أسماء المرجحين للقول الذي يختاره، إلا نادراً.
ه لا يورد الشرنبلالي فيه من الأحكام إلا ما جزم بصحته أهل الترجيح من علماء المذهب.
وإذا كان في المسألة أكثر من قول أو رواية: فإنه يعتمد أحدها مما صححه أهل الترجيح، مختاراً لهذا القول بمرجحات عنده تجعله هو المعتمد في المذهب ،والأقوى، وإن كان هناك من يرى أن الشرنبلالي خالف بذلك المعوّل عليه، أو أنه خالف الأحوط والأولى.
وعلى سبيل المثال لما يعتمده من المرجحات: أن المؤلف في مسألة حكم إقامة المحدث وأذانه ينص في نور الإيضاح على كراهة ذلك، ويُعلل لترجيحه هذا الحكم في شرحه مراقي الفلاح قائلاً: «واتبعت هذه الرواية; لموافقتها نص الحديث : «لا يؤذن إلا متوضى»، وإن صحح عدم كراهة أذان المحدث». اهـ
وعلق على هذا الطحطاوي (١) بأن ما اعتمده المؤلف هو رواية الحسن عن الإمام، وما عَدَلَ عنه هو ظاهر الرواية والمذهب، وهو المصحح. * ومن منهجه رحمه الله في ذكر الخلاف بين علماء المذهب: أنه إذا قوي الخلاف بينهم في التصحيح في المسألة، فإنه يذكر القولين دون ترجيح بينهما، وعلى سبيل المثال: ما جاء في باب سجود التلاوة قال: واختلف التصحيح في وجوبها بالسماع من نائم، ومجنون». اهـ
وفي الكتاب من الأمثلة على ذلك نحو عشر مسائل في مواضع متفرقة، حيث ذكر الخلاف بدون ترجيح، وقد يرجح بينهما في شرحيه.
The author's methodology in Nur al-Idah. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said in the introduction of Nur al-Idah: 'Some close friends asked me — may Allah treat us and them with His hidden kindness — to compile a concise introduction on acts of worship that would bring the scattered rulings in the lengthy works closer to the beginner. So I sought help from Allah Almighty and responded, seeking reward. I only mention what the people of tarjih (preponderance) have definitively deemed correct, without verbosity.' This is from the introduction, and from what I have gathered during my service to the book, the author's methodology can be highlighted in the following points: 1. The book Nur al-Idah is specific to the rulings of acts of worship only: purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and hajj, excluding other fiqh chapters. 2. The author compiled in this book the scattered fiqh issues found in various commentaries and lengthy works, and he did not enumerate them; thereby he made it easy for students of knowledge to find them collected in one place. 3. From the author's methodology in Nur al-Idah, he mentions the rulings of issues in sequence, in a concise and brief manner, without prolongation or verbosity. 4. The author does not mention the name of the proponent from the imams of the madhhab, like Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions, except in few places, nor does he mention the names of those who gave preponderance to the chosen opinion, except rarely. 5. Al-Shurunbulali only includes in it rulings that the people of tarjih from the scholars of the madhhab have definitively deemed correct. 6. If there is more than one opinion or narration in an issue, he adopts one of them which the people of tarjih have deemed correct, choosing this opinion based on preponderating factors that, in his view, make it the relied-upon and strongest opinion in the madhhab, even if there are those who think that al-Shurunbulali thereby contradicted the relied-upon view, or that he contradicted what is more precautionary and preferred. An example of the preponderating factors he relied upon: In the issue of the ruling of a person in a state of minor impurity giving the iqamah and adhan, the author states in Nur al-Idah that it is disliked (makruh), and he explains his preponderance for this ruling in his commentary Maraqi al-Falah saying: 'I followed this narration because it agrees with the text of the hadith: 'None should give the adhan except one who is in a state of wudu', even though the opinion that it is not disliked for a person with minor impurity to give the adhan has been declared authentic.' End quote. Al-Tahtawi commented on this (1) saying that what the author relied upon is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam, and what he deviated from is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) and the madhhab, and that is the correct version. * And from his methodology (may Allah have mercy on him) in mentioning disagreement among the scholars of the madhhab: if the disagreement regarding the correct position in an issue is strong, he mentions both opinions without preponderance between them. For example, what appears in the chapter on sajdah al-tilawah: he said: 'The correct opinion differed regarding its obligation upon hearing from a sleeping person or an insane person.' End quote. In the book there are about ten examples of this in various places, where he mentions the disagreement without preponderance. He may give preponderance between them in his two commentaries.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter analysis of the methodology of al-Shurunbulali in his book Nur al-Idah. The author's stated goal is to provide a concise primer on ibadat (acts of worship) for beginners, extracting rulings from larger works. He restricts content to only those rulings that have been definitively authenticated by the 'people of tarjih' (authoritative later Hanafi jurists who weigh evidence). Among the key methodological features: (1) the book covers only the five pillars of ibadat—taharah, salah, sawm, zakat, hajj; (2) it gathers scattered rulings into one accessible volume; (3) the style is serial and concise; (4) names of early imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) are omitted except rarely, as are names of the tarjih scholars; (5) only rulings 'jazzama bi sihhatihi ahl al-tarjih' are included—those that the later preponderators have affirmed; (6) in cases of strong ikhtilaf, he may mention both sides without preferring one, such as the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah upon hearing from a sleeping or insane person. The passage also illustrates his tarjih method with the example of the adhan of a person without wudu: he follows the narration of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (a nawadir transmission) because it agrees with a hadith, even though the stronger zahir al-riwayah position is that it is not makruh. This shows that he sometimes relies on a weaker transmission if it has stronger textual support, a point criticized by al-Tahtawi. Overall, the student should understand that Nur al-Idah is not a comprehensive fiqh manual but a streamlined text focused on the relied-upon (mu'tamad) positions in ibadat according to the later Hanafi tarjih tradition.

Key Terms
أهل الترجيح (ahl al-tarjih): The scholars who weigh and determine the preponderant (rajih) opinion among multiple narrations or opinions within the Hanafi school.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The established and widely transmitted position from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, as compiled by Imam Muhammad in the six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main criterion for al-Shurunbulali to include a ruling in Nur al-Idah?
A) It must be the most precautionary (ahwat) opinion.
B) It must be from the zahir al-riwayah.
C) It must be a ruling that 'ahl al-tarjih' have definitively deemed correct.
D) It must be the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa alone.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shurunbulali's Nur al-Idah is a curated primer on ibadat that relies on the tarjih of later scholars, not always the primary transmissions of the early Hanafi masters.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Al-Shurunbulali's Tarjih Methodology in Nur al-Idah
Explains author's method of tarjih and use of terminology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Shurunbulali's approach to tarjih and identify the terms he uses to indicate the preferred view.

Core Idea
In Nur al-Idah, the author may prefer a weaker narration if a hadith supports it, even against the madhhab's relied-upon view.

Nur al-Idah is a concise Hanafi fiqh text, but its rulings do not always reflect the standard Zahir al-Riwayah position. This lesson unpacks al-Shurunbulali's methodology: how he performs tarjih, when he presents ikhtilaf without preference, and the specific terms he uses to indicate the corrected or relied-upon view. Understanding this will help you correctly situate Nur al-Idah within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the author's tarjih principle
Recognize that al-Shurunbulali does not blindly follow Zahir al-Riwayah. He chooses an opinion based on his own criteria, even if it is a weaker narration (nawadir).
This is a key difference from many other Hanafi mukhtasar works.
2
Analyze the adhan example
The author rules adhan without wudu as makruh, following the hadith 'لا يؤذن إلا متوضى' even though the school's relied-upon view is that it is not makruh. Note that he declares his tarjih in his commentary.
This shows his methodological priority: hadith over school consensus when evidence is strong.
3
Identify when ikhtilaf is left without tarjih
When the disagreement among scholars about the 'correct' view is strong, al-Shurunbulali mentions both opinions without preferring one. Example: obligation of sajdah tilawah from hearing by a sleeping or insane person.
He may later give tarjih in his commentaries (Maraqi al-Falah).
4
Learn the terminology for the preferred view
The passage lists terms such as 'في الصحيح', 'هو الصحيح', 'في ظاهر الرواية', 'عليه الفتوى' etc. These signal the weight of the ruling in the author's view.
Be aware that 'ظاهر الرواية' refers to the standard school narration, but the author may sometimes deviate from it.

Source Text

منهج المؤلف في نور الإيضاح
الترجيح من علماء المذهب.
صححه
* وإذا كان في المسألة أكثر من قول أو رواية: فإنه يعتمد أحدها مما أهل الترجيح، مختاراً لهذا القول بمرجحات عنده تجعله هو المعتمد في المذهب ،والأقوى، وإن كان هناك من يرى أن الشرنبلالي خالف بذلك المعوّل عليه، أو أنه خالف الأحوط والأولى.
وعلى سبيل المثال لما يعتمده من المرجحات: أن المؤلف في مسألة حكم إقامة المحدث وأذانه ينص في نور الإيضاح على كراهة ذلك، ويُعلل لترجيحه هذا الحكم في شرحه مراقي الفلاح قائلاً: «واتبعت هذه الرواية؛ لموافقتها نص الحديث : «لا يؤذن إلا متوضى»، وإن صحح عدم كراهة أذان المحدث». اهـ
وعلق على هذا الطحطاوي (١) بأن ما اعتمده المؤلف هو رواية الحسن عن الإمام، وما عَدَلَ عنه هو ظاهر الرواية والمذهب، وهو المصحح. * ومن منهجه رحمه الله في ذكر الخلاف بين علماء المذهب: أنه إذا قوي الخلاف بينهم في التصحيح في المسألة، فإنه يذكر القولين دون ترجيح بينهما، وعلى سبيل المثال: ما جاء في باب سجود التلاوة قال:
واختلف التصحيح في وجوبها بالسماع من نائم، ومجنون». اهـ
وفي الكتاب من الأمثلة على ذلك نحو عشر مسائل في مواضع متفرقة، حيث ذكر الخلاف بدون ترجيح، وقد يرجح بينهما في شرحيه.
ولهذا وغيره، فمن الطبيعي أن ترى في هذا الكتاب مسائل يختلف حكمها عما هو في كتاب آخر من كتب المذهب، بسبب وجود اختلاف بين الترجيح عند علماء المذهب، وهذا واضح جداً لمن طالع كتب المذهب الحنفي، وهو موجود أيضاً في كتب غير الحنفية.
٦- نوع المؤلف في نور الإيضاح في التعبير عن الراجح، أو المصحح
هي:
في المذهب، وبالاستقراء وجد أن الألفاظ التي استعملها في ذلك (في الصحيح ـ هو الصحيح - في الأصح ـ في المختار ـ في ظاهر الرواية ـ في صحيح الرواية - في الأظهر - في الظاهر ـ عليه الفتوى ـ عليه الفتوى وأكثر المشايخ، على المعتمد).
-٧- لا يتعرض المؤلف لذكر الأدلة وتعليل الأحكام، إلا قليلاً جداً، وذلك بسبب كون الغرض والمقصود من الكتاب هو إعطاء القارئ ثمرة الأحكام بصورة مختصرة، وأما من أراد الأدلة ووجوه الاستنباط منها فلها موضع آخر في الشروح والمطولات.
جاءت عبارة الكتاب موجزةً سهلة فيها وضوح إلى حد كبير، مع
جمال في الأسلوب، ورشاقة في العبارة.
ومع
هذا فيختلف الحال في فهم عباراته من قارىء إلى آخر بحسب
قوته وضعفه، وبحسب درجة ممارسته لقراءة نصوص المتقدمين، وعليه فلا بد من مراجعة الشروح والحواشي حتى يصح فهم العبارة، ويتم إدراك
الحكم منها، ويبقى للأستاذ المدرس دور كبير في التوجيه والبيان. ٩- جعل المؤلف ضمن كل فصل من فصول الكتاب أرقاماً متسلسلة للمسائل التي يذكرها تحت ذلك الفصل؛ تيسيراً على الطلاب لحفظها،
The author's methodology in Nur al-Idah: Tarjih from the scholars of the madhhab. Corrected. * If there is more than one saying or narration in an issue: he adopts one of them based on what the people of tarjih consider, choosing this saying due to preferences he has that make it the relied-upon and strongest in the madhhab, even if there is someone who thinks that al-Shurunbulali thereby opposed the relied-upon, or that he opposed the more precautionary and preferred. For example of what he adopts from the preferences: In the issue of the ruling on the iqama and adhan of a person with hadath, the author states in Nur al-Idah that it is makruh, and he explains his preference for this ruling in his commentary Maraqi al-Falah saying: “I followed this narration because it agrees with the text of the hadith: ‘No one should give adhan except one who has wudu’, even though it was corrected that the adhan of a person with hadath is not makruh.” End quote. Al-Tahtawi commented on this that what the author adopted is the narration of Hasan from the Imam, and what he deviated from is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) and the madhhab, and it is the corrected view. * From his methodology (may Allah have mercy on him) in mentioning differences among the scholars of the madhhab: that when the difference in correction in an issue is strong among them, he mentions both sayings without preferring between them. For example: what is in the chapter on the prostrations of recitation, he said: “The correction differs regarding its obligation by hearing from a sleeping person or an insane person.” End quote. In the book there are about ten examples of this in different places, where he mentions the difference without tarjih, and he may prefer between them in his commentaries. For this and other reasons, it is natural to see in this book issues whose ruling differs from what is in another book of the madhhab, due to the existence of differences in tarjih among the scholars of the madhhab. This is very clear to one who has studied Hanafi books, and it is also found in non-Hanafi books. 6- The type of expression the author uses in Nur al-Idah for the preferred or corrected view: By induction, the terms he used for that are: (fi al-sahih – huwa al-sahih – fi al-ashah – fi al-mukhtar – fi zahir al-riwaya – fi sahih al-riwaya – fi al-azhar – fi al-zahir – alayhi al-fatwa – alayhi al-fatwa wa akthar al-mashayikh – ala al-mu'tamad). 7- The author does not mention proofs and reasoning of rulings except very rarely, because the purpose and intent of the book is to give the reader the fruit of rulings in a summarized manner. As for one who wants the proofs and ways of reasoning from them, there is another place for that in the commentaries and lengthy works. The wording of the book came concise and easy, with considerable clarity, along with beauty of style and elegance of expression. Nevertheless, understanding its expressions varies from one reader to another according to his strength and weakness, and according to his level of practice in reading the texts of the early scholars. Therefore, it is necessary to consult commentaries and glossaries so that the expression is correctly understood and the ruling is fully grasped. The teacher has a great role in guidance and explanation. 9- The author placed within each chapter of the book sequential numbers for the issues he mentions under that chapter, to facilitate memorization for students.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a front matter section explaining the methodology of Imam al-Shurunbulali in his book Nur al-Idah. The author first clarifies his approach to tarjih (preferring one opinion over others) when multiple opinions exist in the Hanafi madhhab. He adopts an opinion based on his own criteria, which may sometimes lead him to choose a weaker narration over the standard Zahir al-Riwayah. For example, in the issue of adhan by a person without wudu, the author declares it makruh, following the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad over the apparent narration because the hadith 'No adhan except with wudu' supports it. However, al-Tahtawi notes that the madhhab's relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it is not makruh. The author sometimes mentions differences without tarjih when there is strong ikhtilaf among scholars, as in the case of the prostration of recitation being obligatory for one who hears while asleep or insane. This leads to rulings in Nur al-Idah that may differ from other Hanafi works due to varying tarjih. The passage also lists the terms the author uses to indicate the preferred or corrected view, such as 'fi al-sahih' and 'alayhi al-fatwa'. The book is intentionally summary, omitting proofs and reasoning. Despite its clarity, understanding it requires consulting commentaries and a teacher's guidance. The author also numbered issues per chapter to aid students' memorization.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of preferring one legal opinion or narration over another based on certain criteria.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known narration transmitted from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) that forms the core of the school's doctrine.
المصحح (al-musahhah): The corrected or verified view among the Hanafi scholars, often the one relied upon for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the author do when there is strong disagreement among scholars about which opinion is 'correct' (tas-hih) in a particular issue?
A) He always prefers the opinion of the majority of scholars.
B) He mentions both opinions without giving a preference between them.
C) He presents only the opinion that is in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
D) He refrains from mentioning the issue altogether.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shurunbulali's tarjih in Nur al-Idah does not always follow Zahir al-Riwayah; his rulings may differ from other Hanafi works and must be understood in light of his methodology.

Author's Methodology in Nur al-Idah
Methodology and structure of Nur al-Idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the key terms the author uses to indicate the preferred view in Nur al-Idah and explain why he omits proofs.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah is a concise fiqh manual; its preferred views are signaled by special terms like 'al-sahih' and 'alayhi al-fatwa'.

Understanding the author's methodology is essential for correctly interpreting Nur al-Idah. This lesson introduces the terms he uses to indicate the relied-upon position and explains his choice to omit proofs, relying instead on commentaries and teacher guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of Nur al-Idah
Recognize that the book aims to present rulings concisely without detailed proofs.
The author states the book is for giving the reader the result of rulings in a concise manner.
2
Recognize the terms for preferred views
List the terms the author uses to indicate the preferred or corrected view (rajih/musahhah).
Terms include: al-sahih, huwa al-sahih, al-asahh, al-mukhtar, fi zahir al-riwayah, fi sahih al-riwayah, al-azhar, al-zahir, alayhi al-fatwa, alayhi al-fatwa wa akthar al-mashayikh, ala al-mu'tamad.
3
Understand the omission of proofs
Grasp why the author rarely cites proofs: the book is a summary; detailed evidence is found in commentaries.
This avoids overwhelming the beginner reader.
4
Note the numbering system
Observe that each chapter has numbered issues to aid memorization and review.
Example: conditions of prayer are numbered 27, wajibat 18, etc.

The author's methodology in Nur al-Idah. For example, in the conditions and pillars of prayer, he counted twenty-seven conditions; in the obligatory acts of prayer, he counted eighteen obligatory acts; he made the sunan of prayer fifty-one sunan; in the chapter on what invalidates prayer, he counted sixty-eight things; in the chapter on what is disliked for the one praying, he counted seventy-seven things, and so on.

Commentary
This passage is an introduction explaining the author's methodology in Nur al-Idah. The author first notes that rulings in this book may differ from other Hanafi books due to variations in preference (tarjih) among scholars. He then lists the specific terms he uses to indicate the preferred or corrected view in the madhhab, such as 'al-sahih', 'fi zahir al-riwayah', 'alayhi al-fatwa', etc. These terms are important for students to recognize when studying the text. Next, he clarifies that he rarely includes proofs or reasoning, as the book aims to be concise; detailed evidence is found in commentaries. He acknowledges that the concise style requires careful reading and reference to commentaries and a teacher. Finally, he highlights the numbering system within each chapter, which aids memorization and review, giving examples from the prayer section.

Key Terms
في ظاهر الرواية (fi zahir al-riwayah): In the apparent/narrated version (of the Hanafi madhhab's transmitted texts)
عليه الفتوى (alayhi al-fatwa): The ruling on which fatwa is given, i.e., the relied-upon position
الصحيح (al-sahih): The sound/correct view according to the author's tarjih

The Numerical Structure of Nur al-Idah: A Tool for Memorization
Front matter describing author's enumeration method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five categories of prayer rulings enumerated by the author and recall the exact numbers for each.

Core Idea
Systematic enumeration of rulings by count transforms a fiqh text into a memorization anchor.

In this lesson, we explore the author's methodology in Nur al-Idah. Imam al-Shurunbulali organizes the rulings of prayer into numbered lists: shurut, wajibat, sunnan, mufsidat, and makruhat. This approach is not arbitrary; it is a deliberate pedagogical technique to aid students in memorizing and recalling key fiqh principles. Understanding this structure will help you navigate the text and appreciate the matn genre.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five categories
List the categories: shurut (conditions), wajibat (obligations), sunnan (sunnahs), mufsidat (invalidators), and makruhat (disliked acts).
These categories cover the main aspects of prayer rulings.
2
Note the assigned numbers
The author assigns: 27 shurut, 18 wajibat, 51 sunnan, 68 mufsidat, 77 makruhat.
Memorize these numbers as pegs for the content.
3
Understand the purpose
The numbers serve as mnemonic devices, making the text easier to review and recall.
This is a common feature of the matn genre.
4
Apply to a single category
Reflect on the shurut category: what distinguishes a condition from a pillar or obligation? The number 27 helps you know when you have listed all conditions.
The count ensures completeness in learning.

Editor's Methodology for Nur al-Idah
Editorial methodology for Nur al-Idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key editorial steps Dr. Saeed Bakdash followed in producing this edition and explain how he handled textual variants and disputed corrections within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A reliable edition combines manuscript collation, author's own commentary, and transparent treatment of school differences.

A critical edition (tahqiq) of a classical text is more than just printing a manuscript. The editor must compare copies, select the most correct reading, and decide how to present variant rulings. In this passage, Dr. Saeed Bakdash explains his methodology for Nur al-Idah, including how he used the author's own commentary Maraqi al-Falah and how he dealt with cases where Hanafi scholars differed on which position is mufta bihi. Understanding this methodology helps you trust the edition while knowing where the editor exercised judgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's primary task
Read the first paragraph: the editor compared manuscript copies and established the 'chosen text' (nass mukhtar). Note that he only records significant variants that affect meaning or ruling.
The editor did not list every minor difference.
2
Understand the role of Maraqi al-Falah
The editor notes that the author al-Shurunbulali revised some phrases in his commentary. Where the commentary's wording is more precise, the editor sometimes adopts that wording into the matn.
This is why you may see two different wordings in different editions.
3
Analyze the editorial aids added
The editor divided the text into numbered paragraphs and issues, added side headings and diacritical marks, verified hadiths, and wrote brief biographies.
These aids are meant to ease study and reference.
4
Examine the treatment of disputed corrections
The author himself only mentions the strongest position. When there is a strong ikhtilaf in tarjih, the editor adds a note presenting the other corrected view from Hanafi scholars, to show the school's diversity.
This ensures the reader knows that the author's position is not the only valid one.

منهج تحقيق الكتاب
۱- قابلت نص نور الإيضاح على النسخ الخطية التي يسر الله لي جمعها، وأثبت النص المختار الذي تحرّيتُ أنه هو الصواب، أو هو الأصح، ولم أشر إلى فروق النسخ إلا ما كان منها ذا بال، ويؤثر في المعنى والحكم.
وأشير هنا إلى أن المصنف رحمه الله حين شرح هذا المتن في مراقي الفلاح كأنه غير في بعض عبارات نور الإيضاح محرراً مدققاً، كما يحصل هذا لكثير من المصنفين ومن هنا اختلفت النسخ الخطية في بعض العبارات مع ما سجله المؤلف في الأصل الذي شَرَحَه في مراقي الفلاح، وغالب هذا التغيير كان في التعبير، وقد اخترت في بعض المواضع من الكتاب عبارة نور الإيضاح المضمَّن في مراقي الفلاح، والذي نُشر مع
الطبعات، وذلك حين رأيت في العبارة الجديدة زيادة تحرير وتدقيق. ۲۔ جعلت نص الكتاب مفقراً إلى جُملٍ ومسائل متفرقة، وذلك بغية إيضاح النص، ويُسر الوقوف على أحكام المسائل وفروعها، كما وضعتُ
لهذه المسائل والفقرات عناوين جانبية بين معقوفين؛ لإظهارها.

المؤلف ترقيماً ؛ لسهولة الوقوف عليها، ويُسر حفظها ومراجعتها.

منهج تحقيق الكتاب
لفهمه، ومراعاة لحال القارئ الكريم.
ه خرجت ما ذكره المؤلف من أحاديث وأدلة على قلتها، مع ذكر درجة الحديث من أقوال أهل الشأن في ذلك، وقد بلغت الأحاديث التي

Methodology of Editing the Book
29
Methodology of Editing the Book
1. I compared the text of Nur al-Idah with the manuscript copies that Allah made it easy for me to collect, and I established the chosen text that I verified to be correct, or the most correct, and I did not indicate the differences between the copies except what was significant and affected the meaning and ruling.
And I point out here that the author, may Allah have mercy on him, when explaining this matn in Maraqi al-Falah, it seems he changed some phrases of Nur al-Idah with precision and verification, as happens to many authors. Hence the manuscript copies differed in some phrases from what the author recorded in the original that he explained in Maraqi al-Falah, and most of this change was in expression. And I chose in some places of the book the wording of Nur al-Idah that was included in Maraqi al-Falah, which was published with the editions, when I saw in the new wording an increase in refinement and precision. 2. I made the text of the book divided into separate sentences and issues, for the purpose of clarifying the text and facilitating access to the rulings of the issues and their branches. Also I placed for these issues and paragraphs side headings in brackets to show them.
- I numbered the issues for which the author gave specific numbers, and I also assigned numbers to issues occurring within chapters and sections that the author did not number, for ease of reference and ease of memorization and review.
4. I placed medium-level diacritical marks on the text, especially the ambiguous parts, to facilitate understanding and consideration for the esteemed reader.

30
Methodology of Editing the Book
5. I referenced the hadiths and evidences mentioned by the author, despite their scarcity, mentioning the grade of the hadith according to the statements of the specialists in that. The hadiths I worked on in the book amounted to about twenty.
6. I briefly identified the notable personalities mentioned in the book.
I commented on the text of the book in many places with fiqhi notes that I deemed necessary to add, to clarify the text as required by need, often mentioning the source. My main reliance in these comments was on Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Ibn Abidin, and other sources of the Hanafi school. Sometimes I would indicate my quotation from al-Tahtawi with the letter Ta (ط) due to frequent quotation from him. I may not mention the volume and page in my quotations from al-Maraqi and al-Tahtawi because the text is sequential and easy to access.
As for mentioning the mufta bihi in the school and the relied-upon position, it has preceded in the author's methodology that he only mentions what the authorities of tarjih have decisively deemed correct. As for what there is a difference in correction within the school, he chooses what he sees as strongest.
Accordingly: If there is a strong difference in the correction of the ruling of an issue, I tried earnestly to mention the other correction through what the scholars of the school mentioned, to show that what the author mentioned in this book is not the only position in the school, but there is another position equally corrected. These issues are like those in which the author mentioned that the correction differed.
9. I wrote a medium-length biography of the author al-Shurunbulali, for the brother
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is the editor's (Dr. Saeed Bakdash) description of his methodology in producing this edition of Nur al-Idah. He explains that he compared multiple manuscripts and selected the most correct text, noting only significant variant readings. He observes that the author, al-Shurunbulali, when he later wrote his commentary Maraqi al-Falah, seems to have revised some phrases of Nur al-Idah, so the editor sometimes adopted the wording from Maraqi al-Falah for greater precision. The editor structured the text into numbered paragraphs and issues, added side headings, and included diacritical marks to aid comprehension. He verified the few hadiths mentioned in the book, identified personalities, and added extensive footnotes from Hanafi sources like Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, and Ibn Abidin. He clarifies that regarding mufta bihi rulings, the author only mentions the most authoritative position, but where there is a strong difference in correction, the editor provides the alternative view to show the school's diversity. Finally, he includes a biography of al-Shurunbulali.

Key Terms
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical editing of a manuscript text by comparing copies and establishing a reliable version
نص مختار (nass mukhtar): The chosen text that the editor determined to be correct after collation
مراقي الفلاح (Maraqi al-Falah): The commentary written by the author al-Shurunbulali on his own matn Nur al-Idah
مفتى به (mufta bihi): The relied-upon opinion upon which fatwa is given in the school

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the editor do when he found a strong difference in the correction of a ruling within the Hanafi school?
A) He omitted such issues entirely.
B) He chose only the author's original position.
C) He provided the alternative corrected view from Hanafi scholars.
D) He relied on his own ijtihad to resolve the difference.

Key Takeaway
A critical edition of a Hanafi fiqh text should be transparent about manuscript choices and school differences, using the author's own commentary as a key resource.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Understanding the Editor's Methodology in Hanafi Texts
Editor's methodology for fiqh annotation and handling mufta bihi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of a Hanafi editor in clarifying the mufta bihi and how he navigates internal ikhtilaf when verifying rulings.

Core Idea
An editor of a Hanafi text clarifies the school's operative position and its internal diversity to guide accurate fatwa.

This lesson introduces you to the editorial approach used in Nur al-Idah, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. Understanding this methodology is vital because it reflects how centuries of Hanafi scholars have sifted through conflicting opinions to identify the relied-upon ruling (al-mufta bihi). The editor does not merely reproduce the text; he engages with the school's rich tradition of tarjih (preference) and tashih (verification), ensuring that the reader knows not just one view, but the full spectrum of verified positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's tasks
List what the editor explicitly says he did: extracting hadith, grading them, identifying personalities, adding fiqh annotations, and handling mufta bihi. This gives you the anatomy of a scholarly edition.
The editor also flags alternative verified views when a strong ikhtilaf exists.
2
Understand the concept of mufta bihi
The editor follows the author's method: only the view considered correct by the 'people of tarjih' (experts in preference) is presented as the main text. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Mufta bihi is not always the view of the earliest imams; it reflects the cumulative tarjih of the school.
3
Grasp the role of tarjih and tashih
When verification (tashih) differs, the author chooses what he deems strongest. The editor then supplements this by noting that another equally verified view exists, to avoid presenting a single opinion as the only valid one.
This respects the school's internal diversity while maintaining a clear operative ruling.
4
Recognize the sources of authority
The editor's main fiqh sources are Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, and Ibn Abidin. These are later Hanafi works that consolidate the school's positions and are standard references for fatwa.
The editor uses the letter 'ط' for Tahtawi, showing he quoted him heavily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منهج تحقيق الكتاب
لفهمه، ومراعاة لحال القارئ الكريم.
ه خرجت ما ذكره المؤلف من أحاديث وأدلة على قلتها، مع ذكر درجة الحديث من أقوال أهل الشأن في ذلك، وقد بلغت الأحاديث التي خدمتها في الكتاب نحو عشرين حديثاً.
٦ـ عرفت بالأعلام المذكورين في الكتاب بشكل مختصر.
علقت على نص الكتاب في مواضع كثيرة تعليقات فقهية رأيت من الضروري إثباتها؛ لإيضاح النص بما تقتضيه الحاجة، مع ذكر المصدر غالباً، وكان جل اعتمادي في هذه التعليقات على مراقي الفلاح، وحاشية الطحطاوي، وابن عابدين، وغيرها من مصادر المذهب الحنفي، وكنت أحياناً أشير إلى نقلي عن الطحطاوي بحرف الطاء (ط)؛ لكثرة النقل عنه، وقد لا أذكر الجزء والصفحة في نقلي عن المراقي والطحطاوي؛ لتتابع النص، وليسر الوصول إليه.
أما ما يتعلق بذكر المفتى به في المذهب والمعتمد عليه، فقد تقدم في منهج المؤلف أنه لا يذكر إلا ما جزم بصحته أهل الترجيح، وأما ما وقع فيه خلاف في التصحيح في المذهب فيختار ما يراه هو الأقوى.
وعلى هذا: فإذا كان في حكم المسألة خلاف قوي في التصحيح: حاولت جاهداً أن أذكر التصحيح الآخر من خلال ما ذكره علماء المذهب ؛ لبيان أن ما ذكره المؤلف في هذا الكتاب ليس هو القول الوحيد المذهب، بل هناك قول آخر مصحح مثله، ويكون حال هذه المسائل كالتي ذكر المؤلف أنه اختلف التصحيح فيها.
في
٩- ترجمتُ للمصنف الشرنبلالي ترجمة متوسطة؛ حيث إن الأخ الشيخ محمد طلحة بلال قد توسع فيها في مقدمة الطبعة الجديدة التي صدرت في الهند لحاشية الشيخ محمد إعزاز.
Methodology of editing the book, for understanding it, and considering the state of the noble reader. I extracted the ahadith and proofs mentioned by the author, despite their scarcity, while mentioning the grade of the hadith according to the statements of the people of expertise in that. The ahadith that I served in the book amount to about twenty hadiths. 6. I identified the notable persons mentioned in the book in a brief manner. I annotated the text of the book in many places with fiqh commentaries that I deemed necessary to include to clarify the text as required, often mentioning the source. My main reliance in these commentaries was on Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Ibn Abidin, and other sources of the Hanafi school. Sometimes I indicated my quotation from al-Tahtawi with the letter 'T' (ط) due to frequent quotation from him. I may not mention the volume and page in my quotations from al-Maraqi and al-Tahtawi due to the continuity of the text and ease of access. As for mentioning the mufta bihi in the school and the relied-upon position, it has preceded in the author's methodology that he only mentions what the people of tarjih have definitively considered correct. As for what involves disagreement in verification within the school, he chooses what he deems strongest. On this basis: if there is a strong disagreement in verification regarding the ruling of an issue, I tried my best to mention the other verification from what the scholars of the school mentioned to clarify that what the author mentioned in this book is not the only view in the school, but there is another equally verified view, and the status of such issues is like those where the author mentioned that verification differed. 9. I wrote a moderate biography of the author al-Shurunbulali, since the brother Sheikh Muhammad Talha Bilal expanded on it in the introduction to the new edition published in India of the Hashiya of Sheikh Muhammad I'zaz.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is the editor's methodology (manhaj al-tahqiq) for this edition of Nur al-Idah. The editor explains several key aspects of his work. First, he extracted and graded the hadiths cited by the author (al-Shurunbulali), noting their authenticity according to hadith scholars. He identified the notable figures mentioned. He added fiqh annotations based primarily on Hanafi sources: Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, and Ibn Abidin. For mufta bihi (the operative legal position), he follows the author's method of selecting the strongest view, but when there is a strong ikhtilaf in tashih (verification) within the school, he mentions the other verified view to show the school's internal diversity. Finally, he wrote a moderate biography of the author al-Shurunbulali, deferring a more detailed one to another edition.

Key Terms
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The legal ruling that is given as fatwa and relied upon in the school, as determined by the scholars of tarjih.
المعتمد (al-mu'tamad): The relied-upon position in the school, synonymous with mufta bihi.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of preferring one legal opinion over others based on strength of evidence.
تصحيح (tashih): The process of verifying which opinion within the school is correct and reliable for practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the editor mention alternative verified views in his annotations?
A) To reject the author's ruling
B) To show the school's internal diversity while the mufta bihi is still the author's choice
C) To confuse the reader
D) To follow the Shafi'i school

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi text editor not only reproduces the author's words but also contextualizes the mufta bihi within the school's ongoing tradition of tarjih, ensuring the reader knows both the operative ruling and its alternatives.

Evaluating Printed Editions of Classical Hanafi Texts
Front matter discussing editorial methodology and editions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key flaws in printed editions of classical Hanafi texts and select a reliable edition for study.

Core Idea
Not all printed editions of Hanafi classics are reliable; critical textual study is essential.

The Nur al-Idah has been printed many times, but not all editions are equal. Some include extraneous content, others omit entire sections. As a student of Hanafi fiqh, knowing how to assess an edition's reliability is crucial for accurate study. This passage from the editor's introduction gives us a window into the challenges of textual criticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's methodology
Examine what the editor says about his sources. Does he mention using manuscript copies? How many? Does he describe his editorial principles?
A critical edition (taḥqīq) should be based on multiple manuscripts and explain the methodology.
2
Check for completeness
Verify if the edition contains the entire original text, including appendices or supplements by the author. The passage notes that one edition omitted the Zakat and Hajj sections.
Ensure the edition is not abridged or replaced with modern content.
3
Assess added material
Look for diagrams, tables, questions, or treatises by other authors. While helpful, such additions can 'clutter' the edition and distract from the original text.
A 'clean' edition (ṭabʿah ṣāfiyah) contains only the original text with necessary notes.
4
Compare with other editions
Cross-referencing multiple editions helps identify variants and missing parts. The passage praises al-Ata's edition as the best but notes it relied on only one manuscript.
Ideally, use an edition that collates several manuscripts.

الشيخ محمد طلحة بلال قد توسع فيها في مقدمة الطبعة الجديدة التي صدرت في الهند لحاشية الشيخ محمد إعزاز.

طبعات الكتاب
طبع نور الإيضاح طبعات عديدة قديمة وحديثة، مفرداً لوحده، كما نُشر مع مراقي الفلاح، ومع حاشية الشيخ محمد إعزاز الديوبندي، ومع غيرها من الحواشي، في مصر والشام والهند وباكستان وغيرها، ولكن لم أقف إلى الآن على طبعة صافية محققة على نسخ خطية معتمدة.
وأحسن طبعاته بتحقيق الشيخ عبد الجليل العطا، جزاه الله خيراً، وقد اعتمد على المطبوع وعلى نسخة خطية واحدة فقط، وكانت الطبعة الأولى في دمشق، سنة ١٤١٤هـ ، دار النعمان للعلوم، وقد أدخل فيها المحقق مجموعة من الرسوم والأشكال الإيضاحية للوضوء وغيره، وجداول مشجرة لمسائل الكتاب، ووضع مجموعة أسئلة عقب كل فصل ومطلب، ونحو هذا مما اجتهد في إدراجه في الكتاب، كما أنه أقحم معه رسائل عدة لغير الشرنبلالي، مما جعل هذه الطبعة غير صافية، ملاحظات مع علمية عديدة عليها.

Methodology of investigating the book: Sheikh Muhammad Talha Bilal has expanded upon it in the introduction to the new edition published in India of the marginalia of Sheikh Muhammad I'zaz. ***** Editions of the book: Nur al-Idah has been printed in many old and new editions, alone, as well as published with Maraqi al-Falah, and with the marginalia of Sheikh Muhammad I'zaz al-Diyubandi, and with other glosses, in Egypt, Syria, India, Pakistan, and elsewhere. But I have not yet come across a clean critical edition based on reliable manuscript copies. Its best edition is that edited by Sheikh Abdul Jalil al-Ata, may Allah reward him, and it relied on the printed version and only one manuscript copy. The first edition was in Damascus, in 1414 AH, Dar al-Nu'man for Sciences. The editor included in it a set of diagrams and illustrative figures for wudu and other things, and tree-chart tables for the book's issues, and placed a set of questions after each chapter and section, and similar things that he exerted effort to include in the book. Also, he inserted several treatises by others than al-Sharnublali, which made this edition not clean (pure). There are many academic observations on it. Also, I alert here that the edition of Nur al-Idah by Sheikh Muhammad Ali Idlibi, published by Dar al-Falah in Aleppo, 1st edition 1410/1 AH – I alert that this edition is devoid of the author's supplement regarding the book of Zakat and Hajj, and instead modern writing on Zakat and Hajj has been placed, with the insightful commentator noting that in his introduction.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is front matter from Nur al-Idah, where the author discusses the editorial methodology and printed editions of the book. The author first notes that Sheikh Muhammad Talha Bilal has expanded on the methodology in his introduction to the new Indian edition of the commentary by Sheikh Muhammad I'zaz. Then he turns to the history of the book's editions: Nur al-Idah has been printed many times, alone or with commentaries like Maraqi al-Falah, but none is a fully critical edition based on verified manuscripts. He praises the edition by Sheikh Abdul Jalil al-Ata as the best so far, but critiques it for relying on only one manuscript, adding extraneous diagrams and tables, and including treatises by other authors, which compromises its purity. He also warns about the edition by Sheikh Muhammad Ali Idlibi, which omits the author's own completion of the Zakat and Hajj sections and replaces them with modern content. This highlights the importance of using reliable, authentic editions when studying classical Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
تحقيق (taḥqīq): Critical editing of a manuscript based on comparing multiple copies and verifying authenticity.
طبعة صافية (ṭabʿah ṣāfiyah): A clean, pure edition that contains only the original text without extraneous additions.
نسخ خطية معتمدة (nusakh khaṭṭiyyah muʿtamadah): Reliable manuscript copies used as sources for critical editions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A reliable edition of a classical text is one based on multiple manuscripts, complete, and free from extraneous insertions or substitutions.

Editions of Nur al-Idah and Their Reliability
Describes print history and critical evaluation of editions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of different printed editions of Nur al-Idah and identify the criteria for a critical edition in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Not all printed editions of Nur al-Idah are equal; a critical edition must rely on multiple manuscripts and avoid extraneous inclusions.

As a student of Hanafi fiqh, you will often rely on texts like Nur al-Idah. However, the printed editions available vary greatly in quality. This lesson examines the landscape of editions, highlighting the shortcomings of even the best ones and teaching you what to look for in a reliable text. This is not just bibliographic trivia—it affects the accuracy of your knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main editions mentioned
List the editions of Nur al-Idah, Maraqi al-Falah, and Imdad al-Fattah mentioned in the passage, noting their editors and publication details.
Focus on the editions by al-'Ata, Idlibi, and others.
2
Analyze the author's criticism
Understand why the author is dissatisfied even with the best edition: it relies on only one manuscript and includes treatises not by al-Shurunbulali.
These are the two main flaws.
3
Assess the completeness issue
Note that some editions omit the author's completion (zakat and hajj) and substitute modern material, which can mislead students.
The Idlibi edition is cited as an example.
4
Evaluate the criteria for a good edition
From the criticism, derive what a critical edition should have: multiple manuscripts, no added foreign material, complete original text.
This forms the basis for evaluating any edition.
5
Apply to your own study
Determine which edition you would prioritize if you were studying Nur al-Idah, and justify your choice based on the criteria.
Consider the trade-offs between availability and purity.

طبع نور الإيضاح طبعات عديدة قديمة وحديثة، مفرداً لوحده، كما نُشر مع مراقي الفلاح، ومع حاشية الشيخ محمد إعزاز الديوبندي، ومع غيرها من الحواشي، في مصر والشام والهند وباكستان وغيرها، ولكن لم أقف إلى الآن على طبعة صافية محققة على نسخ خطية معتمدة. وأحسن طبعاته بتحقيق الشيخ عبد الجليل العطا، جزاه الله خيراً، وقد اعتمد على المطبوع وعلى نسخة خطية واحدة فقط، وكانت الطبعة الأولى في دمشق، سنة ١٤١٤هـ ، دار النعمان للعلوم، وقد أدخل فيها المحقق مجموعة من الرسوم والأشكال الإيضاحية للوضوء وغيره، وجداول مشجرة لمسائل الكتاب، ووضع مجموعة أسئلة عقب كل فصل ومطلب، ونحو هذا مما اجتهد في إدراجه في الكتاب، كما أنه أقحم معه رسائل عدة لغير الشرنبلالي، مما جعل هذه الطبعة غير صافية، ملاحظات علمية عديدة عليها. كما أنبه هنا إلى أن طبعة نور الإيضاح التي للشيخ محمد علي إدلبي، نشر دار الفلاح بحلب، ط١٤١٠/١هـ، أنبه إلى أن هذه الطبعة خالية من تتمة المؤلف الخاصة بكتاب الزكاة والحج، وقد وضع بدلاً عنها كتابة حديثة في الزكاة والحج، مع تنبيه المعلق الفاضل إلى ذلك في مقدمته. أما مراقي الفلاح شرح نور الإيضاح للشرنبلالي، فقد ذكر في فهرس الظاهرية للفقه الحنفي أنه تم طبعه قديماً في المطبعة الوهبية سنة ١٢٧٦هـ، وسنة ١٢٨١هـ، وفي المطبعة الخيرية سنة ١٣٠٣هـ، والميمنية سنة ١٣٠٥هـ، والجمالية سنة ١٣٢٩هـ، كما طبع بحاشية الطحطاوي سنة ١٣٠١هـ، وله طبعة قديمة مصححة في القاهرة، سنة ١٣٦٧هـ، وقد انتشرت عنها صورة في دار المعرفة ببيروت. وكذلك فإن طبعاته الحديثة عديدة، وأحسنها طبعة الشيخ عبد الجليل العطا، ط ١٤١١/هـ ، دار النعمان، دمشق. وهكذا تم أيضاً طبع إمداد الفتاح أكثر من طبعة، إحداها بإخراج الشيخ عبد الكريم العطا وليس فيها تتمة المؤلف، وهي كتاب الزكاة والحج، ط١، سنة ١٤٢١هـ، دار إحياء التراث العربي، بيروت، والثانية بإخراج بشار بكري عرابي بدون ذكر الدار للنشر.
Nur al-Idah has many old and new editions, published alone, as well as with Maraqi al-Falah, with the gloss of Shaykh Muhammad I'zaz al-Diyubandi, and with other glosses, in Egypt, the Levant, India, Pakistan, and elsewhere. But I have not yet found a clean edition verified against reliable manuscript copies. The best edition is that of Shaykh 'Abd al-Jalil al-'Ata, may Allah reward him. He relied on printed versions and only one manuscript copy. The first edition was in Damascus, 1414 AH, Dar al-Nu'man li al-'Ulum. The editor included a set of diagrams and explanatory figures for wudu and other topics, and branching tables for the book's topics, and placed a set of questions after each chapter and section, and so on, which he endeavored to incorporate into the book. He also included several treatises not by al-Shurunbulali, making this edition impure, with many scholarly notes. I also draw attention to the fact that the edition of Nur al-Idah by Shaykh Muhammad 'Ali Idlibi, published by Dar al-Falah in Aleppo, 2nd edition 1410/1 AH, is devoid of the author's completion regarding zakat and hajj. Instead, modern writing on zakat and hajj was placed, with the commentator noting this in his introduction. As for Maraqi al-Falah, the commentary on Nur al-Idah by al-Shurunbulali, it is mentioned in the Dhahiriyya index of Hanafi fiqh that it was printed in the Wahbiyya printing house in 1276 AH, 1281 AH, in the Khayriyya printing house in 1303 AH, al-Mimaniyya in 1305 AH, al-Jamaliyya in 1329 AH, and also printed with the gloss of al-Tahawi in 1301 AH. It has an old corrected edition in Cairo in 1367 AH, a reproduction of which spread in Dar al-Ma'rifa in Beirut. Its modern editions are many, the best being the edition of Shaykh 'Abd al-Jalil al-'Ata, 1411/1 AH, Dar al-Nu'man, Damascus. Similarly, Imdad al-Fattah has been printed more than once, one edition by Shaykh 'Abd al-Karim al-'Ata without the author's completion (the books of zakat and hajj), 1st edition, 1421 AH, Dar Ihya' al-Turath al-'Arabi, Beirut, and the second by Bashar Bakri 'Arabi without mentioning the publisher.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This is a front-matter section describing the print history of Nur al-Idah and its associated works. The author notes that despite many prints, a truly critical edition based on multiple manuscripts is still absent. The best available edition (by Shaykh 'Abd al-Jalil al-'Ata) is praised but criticized for relying on only one manuscript and including additional treatises not by the original author, making it 'impure'. Another edition (by Idlibi) lacks the author's completion on zakat and hajj, substituting modern material. The commentary Maraqi al-Falah has numerous historical prints; the best modern one is also by al-'Ata. Imdad al-Fattah has incomplete editions. This information is crucial for students who wish to rely on accurate texts for their studies. It also highlights the importance of textual criticism in the Hanafi tradition, as the author expresses a desire for a pure, verified edition.

Key Terms
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): A primer in Hanafi fiqh by al-Shurunbulali, used as a standard textbook.
مراقي الفلاح (Maraqi al-Falah): The commentary on Nur al-Idah by the same author, al-Shurunbulali.
إمداد الفتاح (Imdad al-Fattah): A gloss (hashiya) on Maraqi al-Falah by al-Tahawi.
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical edition, based on collation of multiple manuscripts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The quality of a printed edition directly impacts the accuracy of your fiqh knowledge; always seek critical editions based on multiple manuscripts.

Bibliographic overview of editions and manuscripts of Nur al-Idah and its commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key printed editions and manuscript sources of Nur al-Idah and evaluate their reliability for scholarly study.

Core Idea
The critical edition of a fiqh text depends on identifying the earliest and most accurate manuscripts and printed editions.

This passage from the introduction to a modern edition of Nur al-Idah provides a bibliographic overview of the printed editions and manuscripts used. While not a legal ruling, it equips you with the tools to assess the reliability of texts you will encounter in your study of Hanafi fiqh. Understanding this methodology is essential for rigorous scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the printed editions listed
Note the various old press editions (al-Wahbiyya, al-Khayriyya, etc.) and the modern best edition.
The best modern edition is by Shaykh 'Abd al-Jalil al-'Ata (Dar al-Nu'man, Damascus).
2
Distinguish between base text and commentary
Recognize that Maraqi al-Falah is a commentary on Nur al-Idah, and Imdad al-Fattah is a supercommentary.
Understanding the relationship helps in choosing the right text for study.
3
Recognize the manuscript basis
The editor used over eleven manuscripts, including two oldest from Tunisia (1062 AH and 1073 AH).
The unreliability of the reported autograph manuscript highlights the need for verified sources.
4

The editor attempted to locate the author's autograph but failed; he relied on early copies and multiple witnesses.
Critical edition methodology requires checking multiple sources and noting limitations.
5

ذكر أصحاب فهرس آل البيت(۱) (۱۱۱) نسخة خطية من كتاب نور الإيضاح، وذكروا أن نسخة منها بخط المؤلف موجودة في المكتبة المركزية في تيرانا بألبانيا، وبناء على ذلك أرسلت عن طريق أكثر من أخ من طلاب العلم من أهل ألبانيا لتصويرها لكن أكدوا لى جميعاً بعد مراجعتهم أنها غير موجودة. كما ذكر أصحاب الفهرس أيضاً أقدم نسختين من الكتاب في دار الكتب الوطنية بتونس، الأولى بتاريخ ١٠٦٢هـ، أي في حياة المؤلف، والثانية بتاريخ ١٠٧٣هـ، أي بعد أربع سنين من وفاة المؤلف، وقد يسر الله لي الحصول على صورة منهما، وذلك بسعاية وكرم سعادة الأستاذ الدكتور فضيلة الشيخ محمد الحبيب الهيلة من أهل تونس الخضراء، من [؟] كانت ولا زالت تربطني به مودة ومحبة وتقدير واحترام أيام مقامي بمكة المكرمة بجامعة أم القرى.
كما يسر الله لي تصوير أكثر من عشر نسخ خطية أخرى من نور الإيضاح مختلفة الحال، وثلاث نسخ من شرحه مراقي الفلاح المضمن فيه نور الإيضاح مع التتمة لكتاب الزكاة والحج، إحداها نسخت في حياة المؤلف سنة ١٠٥٦هـ.
(۱) الفهرس الشامل ٣٣٠/١١.
Editions of the Book (1) As for Maraqi al-Falah, the commentary on Nur al-Idah by al-Shurunbulali, it is mentioned in the al-Zahiriyya index for Hanafi fiqh (1) that it was printed old in the al-Wahbiyya press in 1276 AH, and 1281 AH, and in the al-Khayriyya press in 1303 AH, and al-Maymaniyya in 1305 AH, and al-Jamaliyya in 1329 AH, and it was printed with the commentary of al-Tahtawi in 1301 AH, and it has an old corrected edition in Cairo, in 1367 AH, and a copy of it spread in Dar al-Ma'rifa in Beirut. And likewise its modern editions are numerous, and the best of them is the edition of Shaykh 'Abd al-Jalil al-'Ata, print 1411/1 AH, Dar al-Nu'man, Damascus. Thus also Imdad al-Fattah was printed in more than one edition, one of them produced by Shaykh 'Abd al-Karim al-'Ata without the author's completion, which is the book of Zakat and Hajj, 1st ed., 1421 AH, Dar Ihya' al-Turath al-'Arabi, Beirut, and the second produced by Bashar Bakri 'Arabi without mentioning the publishing house. ***** Manuscripts Relied Upon in the Critical Edition Manuscripts Relied Upon in the Critical Edition, The owners of the Fihris Al al-Bayt (1) mentioned (111) manuscript copies of the book Nur al-Idah, and they mentioned that one copy in the author's handwriting exists in the Central Library in Tirana, Albania, and based on that I sent via more than one brother of knowledge seekers from Albania to photograph it, but they all confirmed to me after checking that it does not exist. The index owners also mentioned the two oldest copies of the book in the National Library in Tunisia, the first dated 1062 AH, i.e. during the author's life, and the second dated 1073 AH, i.e. four years after the author's death, and Allah enabled me to obtain a copy of them, through the assistance and generosity of His Excellency Professor Dr. al-Fadil Shaykh Muhammad al-Habib al-Hayla from the green Tunisia, from [؟] there was and still is a friendship, love, appreciation and respect between me and him during my stay in Mecca at Umm al-Qura University. Also Allah enabled me to photograph more than ten other manuscript copies of Nur al-Idah in varying condition, and three copies of its commentary Maraqi al-Falah which includes Nur al-Idah with the completion of the book of Zakat and Hajj, one of which was copied during the author's life in 1056 AH. (1) The Comprehensive Index 11/330.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is part of the introduction to a modern critical edition of Nur al-Idah. The editor, Dr. Saeed Bakdash, provides a bibliographic overview of the printed editions of Maraqi al-Falah (the famous commentary on Nur al-Idah by al-Shurunbulali) and its supercommentary Imdad al-Fattah. He notes the various old lithographic prints and superior modern editions. Then he discusses the manuscript sources used for his critical edition. He references the Fihris Al al-Bayt which records 111 manuscripts of Nur al-Idah, including one purportedly in the author's hand in Albania, but it could not be located. The two oldest manuscripts are in the National Library of Tunisia, one from the author's lifetime (1062 AH) and one from shortly after his death (1073 AH). The editor obtained copies of these and over ten other manuscripts, plus three copies of Maraqi al-Falah. This background establishes the scholarly methodology of the critical edition.

Key Terms
مراقي الفلاح (Maraqi al-Falah): The famous commentary on Nur al-Idah by al-Shurunbulali, widely used in Hanafi fiqh instruction.
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): A foundational text in Hanafi fiqh by al-Shurunbulali, covering ibadat (acts of worship).
إمداد الفتاح (Imdad al-Fattah): A supercommentary on Maraqi al-Falah, written by al-Shurunbulali as a completion of the work.

Manuscript Sources for Hanafi Fiqh: Maraqi al-Falah and Daw' al-Misbah
Listing two manuscript copies used for verification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of manuscript copies (Maraqi al-Falah and Daw' al-Misbah) in the verification of Nur al-Idah and explain their relationship.

Core Idea
Daw' al-Misbah is an abridgment of Maraqi al-Falah, not a separate work; both are key sources for verifying Nur al-Idah.

In studying Hanafi fiqh, particularly the text Nur al-Idah by al-Shurunbulali, scholars rely on manuscript copies and commentaries to establish the correct text. This passage from the verified edition lists two important manuscripts used by the editor. Understanding the chain of transmission helps us trust the accuracy of the fiqh rulings we study.

Guided Path
1

2

3
Evaluate the significance for verification
Understand that these manuscripts were primary sources for the editor, with Daw' al-Misbah frequently cited by later scholars like al-Tahtawi as 'al-Sayyid'.

١٣٧٣هـ
The manuscript copies relied upon in verification. 37. 12- A copy of Maraqi al-Falah without date of copying, consisting of 131 folios, each page 22 lines, original preserved in the Saqizli Library in Medina, in the King Abdulaziz Library, and it is a copy heavily annotated with comments and additions. 13- Among the copies I relied upon in verification is also a manuscript copy of the book: Daw' al-Misbah, commentary on Nur al-Idah by Allamah Abu al-Su'ud al-Husayni al-Misri Muhammad bin Ali (d. 1172 AH), author of the valuable marginalia printed on the commentary of al-Kanz by Mulla Miskeen, and he stated in his introduction that he abridged it from Maraqi al-Falah by the author. Al-Tahtawi frequently quoted from him in his marginalia on Maraqi al-Falah, mentioned him among his sources in his introduction, and attributes to him saying: 'Ended by Sayyid - said by Sayyid - mentioned by Sayyid - in al-Sayyid', and I collated a number of texts and found them in it. Commentary
This passage is from the introduction to the edited edition of Nur al-Idah. It describes the manuscript sources used for verification. The first (copy #12) is a manuscript of Maraqi al-Falah by Imam al-Shurunbulali, heavily annotated, housed in the Saqizli Library (now part of King Abdulaziz Library) in Medina. The second (copy #13) is a commentary on Nur al-Idah titled Daw' al-Misbah by Abu al-Su'ud al-Husayni, who abridged it from Maraqi al-Falah. This commentary was frequently cited by al-Tahtawi in his own supercommentary on Maraqi al-Falah. The editor notes that al-Tahtawi refers to this work simply as 'al-Sayyid' (the Sayyid). These manuscript details establish the chain of transmission for the Hanafi fiqh text.

Key Terms

ضوء المصباح (Daw' al-Misbah): A supercommentary on Nur al-Idah by Abu al-Su'ud al-Husayni, abridged from Maraqi al-Falah.

Reading a Hanafi Colophon
Colophon detailing manuscript copies used for verification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and interpret the key elements of a Hanafi manuscript colophon.

Core Idea
A colophon preserves the chain of transmission and dates, ensuring textual integrity.

A colophon is more than a closing note — it is a legal guarantee of textual authenticity. In the Hanafi tradition, knowing the chain of transmission (sanad) of a text is essential for establishing its reliability. This lesson teaches you to parse the colophon of Nur al-Idah, a core Hanafi fiqh text, and understand its significance for scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and author
Locate the title of the work (Nur al-Idah) and the author's name (Hasan ibn Ammar al-Shurunbulali). This establishes the text's identity.
2
Find the completion date (tārīkh al-ta’līf)
The author states when he finished writing: Jumada al-Ula 1035 AH. This date helps date the original composition.
3
Find the copyist’s note
The copyist mentions that this manuscript was copied from the author's autograph. This increases the manuscript's authority.
Copying from the original autograph is the highest level of reliability.
4
Identify the copy date (tārīkh al-naskh)
Two copy dates are given: 1062 AH and 1073 AH (different copies). This shows when the copies were made.
The closer the copy date is to the author’s death, the more valuable it is.
5
Understand the role of multiple copies
The critical edition used multiple manuscript copies to reconstruct the original text. Variants are resolved by comparing them.
This is standard methodology (tahqiq) in Islamic textual scholarship.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

نور الإيضاح نسخة تونس بتاريخ 1062 هـ
وقال مؤلفه: تمت تأليفه المبارك رابع عشر في جمادى الأول سنة خمس وثلاثين وألف
ونسخت هذه النسخة من نسخة بخط مؤلفها حسن بن عمار بن علي
الشرق بالالي الوفاء الحنيفي وكان الفراغ في عام المبارك المتمم عشرين من شوال سنة أربع وأربعين

The manuscript copies relied upon in the verification. Nur al-Idah, Tunis copy dated 1062 AH. Its author said: Its blessed composition was completed on the fourteenth of Jumada al-Ula in the year 1035 AH. This copy was made from a copy in the handwriting of its author, Hasan ibn Ammar ibn Ali al-Sharq al-Ali al-Wafa al-Hanafi. The completion was in the blessed year, the twentieth of Shawwal, in the year 1044 AH. Nur al-Idah, Tunis copy dated 1073 AH, the penultimate folio.

Commentary
This passage is a colophon (front matter) listing the manuscript copies used by the editor (Dr. Saeed Bakdash) in his critical edition of Nur al-Idah. It mentions two Tunisian copies: one dated 1062 AH and another dated 1073 AH. The passage also quotes the author, Hasan ibn Ammar al-Shurunbulali, stating that he completed the original work in 1035 AH. The copyist notes that this particular copy was transcribed from the author's own autograph. This is typical of Islamic manuscript tradition, where copyists preserve the chain of transmission and dates of copying.

Key Terms
نسخة خطية (nuskhah khattiyyah): A handwritten manuscript copy of a work
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical edition of a classical text based on multiple manuscripts
تاريخ التأليف (tārīkh al-ta’līf): The date when the author finished composing the work
تاريخ النسخ (tārīkh al-naskh): The date when a particular manuscript copy was made

The Role of Manuscript Verification in Hanafi Fiqh Texts
Editorial manuscript notes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two manuscript copies of Nur al-Idah used in Dr. Bakdash's critical edition and explain why manuscript dating and provenance matter for reliable Hanafi fiqh study.

Core Idea
Knowing a text's manuscript lineage is essential for reliable fiqh rulings.

This passage, from the critical edition of Nur al-Idah, lists the manuscript copies relied upon by the editor. While it appears to be mere bibliography, understanding the chain of manuscript transmission is a foundational skill for the Hanafi jurist. A ruling is only as strong as its text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two manuscripts
Locate the two manuscript copies mentioned: one from Medina (dated 1183 AH) and one from the Dhahiriya library (dated 1261 AH). Note their dates and provenances.
The earlier copy (1183 AH) is closer to the author's time and likely more reliable.
2
Understand the editor's purpose
The editor lists these manuscripts to demonstrate his methodology: he compared multiple copies to produce a critical text. This is standard tahqiq practice.
Manuscript comparison helps eliminate scribal errors and variations.
3
Apply to Hanafi fiqh study
When studying a fiqh text, always check which manuscript tradition is being used. A corrupted text can lead to incorrect rulings. The reliability of a fatwa depends on the accuracy of its source.
Contemporary printed editions often rely on multiple manuscripts; knowing this builds scholarly rigor.

Understanding the Purpose of Nur al-Idah
Author explains the motivation and methodology for writing a concise Hanafi fiqh manual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose and guiding principle of Nur al-Idah and identify the category of fiqh it covers.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah is a concise beginner's guide to Hanafi worship rulings, based only on the most authoritative positions.

In this lesson, we examine the author's own introduction to Nur al-Idah. The author, Hasan al-Shurunbulali, explains why he wrote the book and the methodology he followed. This will help you understand the scope and authority of the rulings you will study in subsequent lessons.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's subject matter
Read the first line after the basmalah where the author mentions what the book covers: specifically 'acts of worship' (al-‘ibādāt). Note the five components listed later: purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and Hajj.
The book does not cover transactions (mu‘āmalāt).
2
Understand the author's methodology
The author states he only includes what 'the people of tarjīḥ' have confirmed as correct. This means the rulings are the relied-upon (muftā bihī) positions in the Hanafi school, not the author's own ijtihād.
This ensures the book is a reliable summary for beginners.
3
Analyze the title
The title 'Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah' means 'The Light of Clarification and the Salvation of Souls'. Consider how each part reflects the book's purpose: clarifying scattered issues and leading to spiritual success.
4
Place the book in historical context
The footnote tells us the book was written in stages, with commentaries later. This shows the author's careful approach and the book's importance as a foundational text.
The author first wrote on purification, prayer, fasting in 1032 AH, then added zakat and Hajj later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مقدمة المؤلّف
الحمد لله رب العالمين، والصلاةُ والسلام على سيدنا محمد خاتم النبيين وعلى آله الطاهرين وصحابته أجمعين.
قال العبد الفقير إلى مولاه الغني أبو الإخلاص حسن الوفائي الشرنبلالي الحنفي عفا الله عنه :
إنه قد التمس مني بعض الأخلاء - عامَلَنا الله وإياهم بلطفه الخَفِي - أن أعمل مقدمة في العبادات (۱) ، تُقرَّبُ على المبتدئ ما تشتت من المسائل في المطولات، فاستعن بالله تعالى وأجبته طالباً للثواب، ولا أذكر إلا ما جَزَمَ بصحته أهلُ الترجيح، من غير إطناب، وسميته: «نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح».
والله أسألُ أن ينفع به عباده، ويُديم به الإفادة.
(۱) كتب المؤلف أولاً أحكام الطهارة والصلاة والصيام، وذلك سنة ١٠٣٢هـ، ثم شرحه شرحين سمى الأول منهما وهو الأكبر : إمداد الفتـاح»، وعدد أوراقـه ـ كما قال المؤلف - ٣٦٠ ورقة، وانتهى منه سنة ١٠٤٦هـ، وسمى الثاني وهو مختصر من الأول : مراقي الفلاح ، وعدد أوراقه ١٤٥ ورقة وكانت المدة بين الشرحين نحواً من سبع سنوات ونصف، كما قال الطحطاوي [؟]، ثم أتم بعد ذلك ـ أي بعد سنة ١٠٥٤ هـ ـ أحكام الزكاة والحج، فكملت العبادات، ولكن لم يشرح التتمة.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Author's introduction. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad, the seal of the prophets, and upon his pure family and all his companions. Said the servant in need of his Rich Lord, Abu al-Ikhlas Hasan al-Wafai al-Shurunbulali al-Hanafi, may Allah forgive him: Indeed, some close friends - may Allah treat us and them with His hidden kindness - requested from me that I compose an introduction on acts of worship, which would bring closer to the beginner what is scattered of issues in the lengthy works. So I sought help from Allah Almighty and answered them seeking reward. I will mention only what the people of tarjih have confirmed as correct, without verbosity. I named it 'Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah'. I ask Allah to benefit His servants with it and perpetuate benefit through it. (1) The author first wrote the rulings of purification, prayer, and fasting in the year 1032 AH, then commented on it with two commentaries: the first and larger he named 'Imdad al-Fattah', its number of folios - as the author said - 360 folios, completed in 1046 AH. The second, which is an abridgment of the first, he named 'Maraqi al-Falah', its folios 145. The period between the two commentaries was about seven and a half years, as al-Tahawi said [?]. Then after that - i.e. after the year 1054 AH - he completed the rulings of zakat and Hajj, thus completing the acts of worship, but he did not comment on the supplement.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This is the author's introduction to his book Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah. The author is Hasan al-Shurunbulali, a Hanafi scholar from Egypt (d. 1659 CE). He begins with the basmalah, praise of Allah, and blessings on the Prophet and his family. He then explains the reason for writing: some friends asked him to produce a concise work on acts of worship (al-‘ibadat) that would make the scattered rulings found in longer works accessible to beginners. He emphasizes that he only includes rulings that the 'people of tarjih' (those competent to weigh evidences) have deemed sound. This reflects the Hanafi tradition of relying on the mufta bihi (operative) positions. He names the book 'Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah' (The Light of Clarification and the Salvation of Souls). The footnote provides additional biographical information: he first wrote the sections on purification, prayer, and fasting in 1032 AH, then authored two commentaries: a larger one called Imdad al-Fattah (360 folios) and an abridged one called Maraqi al-Falah (145 folios). Later, after 1054 AH, he added zakat and Hajj, completing the full coverage of worship acts, though he did not write commentaries on the later additions.

Key Terms
مقدمة (muqaddimah): The introductory section of the book outlining its purpose and scope.
العبادات (al-‘ibādāt): Acts of worship; the legal category comprising purification, prayer, fasting, zakat, and Hajj.
أهل الترجيح (ahl al-tarjīḥ): Scholars qualified to weigh conflicting evidences and determine the preferred (rajih) ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To present new ijtihad on all fiqh issues
B) To compile a concise work on acts of worship for beginners based on relied-upon rulings
C) To refute the views of other madhhabs
D) To write a comprehensive commentary on the Quran

Key Takeaway
Nur al-Idah provides beginners with concise, authoritative Hanafi rulings on acts of worship, selected by the scholars of tarjīḥ.

Author's Introduction: The Purpose and Method of Nūr al-Īḍāḥ
Author states motivation, method, and title of the work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the author's motivation, identify the scope of Nūr al-Īḍāḥ, and state the criterion for selecting rulings in this work.

Core Idea
Nūr al-Īḍāḥ is a beginner-friendly primer on ʿibādāt, relying only on the preponderant (rājiḥ) Ḥanafī positions.

Al-Shurunbulālī wrote this concise work to help beginners master the essential rulings of worship without being overwhelmed by the lengthy discussions in larger fiqh books. He focuses on the muʿtamad positions approved by ahl al-tarjīḥ, ensuring reliability. This lesson explores the author's intent and the work's enduring value as a teaching text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his motivation
Read the opening: who is the author and why did he write this work?
The author is Abu al-Ikhlas Hasan al-Shurunbulali al-Hanafi. He was asked by friends to prepare an introduction on acts of worship.
2
Define the scope of the work
What does the author say he will include? What area of fiqh does he cover?
He mentions 'muqaddima fi al-ʿibādāt' – an introduction on acts of worship, not all of fiqh.
3
Explain the selection criterion
What does 'j-zama bi-sihhatihi ahl al-tarjīḥ' mean? Why is this important for a beginner?
He only includes what the people of tarjīḥ have affirmed as correct, i.e., the muʿtamad positions. This protects the beginner from weak or minority views.
4
Interpret the title
What does 'Nūr al-Īḍāḥ wa Najāt al-Arwāḥ' signify?
‘The Light of Clarification and the Salvation of Souls’ – the book is meant to illuminate and bring salvation.
5
Reflect on the author's dua
What is the author's hope for the work?
He asks Allah to benefit His servants through it and to perpetuate benefit.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله رب العالمين، والصلاةُ والسلام على سيدنا محمد خاتم النبيين وعلى آله الطاهرين وصحابته أجمعين.

إنه قد التمس مني بعض الأخلاء - عامَلَنا الله وإياهم بلطفه الخَفِي - أن أعمل مقدمة في العبادات، تُقرَّبُ على المبتدئ ما تشتت من المسائل في المطولات، فاستعن بالله تعالى وأجبته طالباً للثواب، ولا أذكر إلا ما جَزَمَ بصحته أهلُ الترجيح، من غير إطناب، وسميته: «نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح».

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad, the seal of the prophets, and upon his pure family and all his companions. The poor slave in need of his Rich Lord, Abu al-Ikhlas Hasan al-Wafa'i al-Shurunbulali al-Hanafi, may Allah forgive him, said: Indeed, some close friends asked me—may Allah treat us and them with His subtle kindness—to prepare an introduction on acts of worship, which would make easy for the beginner what is scattered in the lengthy works. So I sought help from Allah Almighty and responded to them seeking reward. I mention only what the people of tarjih have affirmed as correct, without verbosity, and I named it 'Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah.' And I ask Allah to benefit His servants through it and to perpetuate benefit.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This is the author's introduction. Al-Shurunbulali explains that he wrote this work at the request of some friends who wanted a concise yet authoritative summary of the rulings of worship (ʿibādāt) geared toward beginners. He limits himself to reliably preponderant positions (j-zama bi-sihhatihi ahl al-tarjīḥ), avoiding lengthy discussions, and gives the book the title 'The Light of Clarification and the Salvation of Souls.' The phrase 'people of tarjīḥ' refers to those Ḥanafī scholars who weighed and selected the strongest rulings within the school, ensuring the work reflects the relied-upon positions (muʿtamad). The author, Abū al-Ikhlāṣ Ḥasan al-Shurunbulālī al-Ḥanafī (d. 1069 AH), was a prominent Ḥanafī jurist, known for his works such as this and its commentary 'Marāqī al-Falāḥ.'

Key Terms
مقدمة (muqaddimah): An introductory work covering the essentials of a subject; here specifically on the fiqh of worship.
أهل الترجيح (ahl al-tarjīḥ): Scholars who determine the preponderant (rājiḥ) ruling among differing opinions within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Nūr al-Īḍāḥ is a concise beginner's primer on acts of worship that presents only the preponderant (rājiḥ) Ḥanafī positions, making it a trusted starting point for learning fiqh.
