The Colophon of Nur al-Idah
Author's concluding remarks and completion date

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose and content of a classical Hanafi fiqh colophon and identify the completion date of Nur al-Idah.

Core Idea
A colophon authenticates a work by recording its completion date and the author's prayers.

The conclusion of a classical fiqh text often contains more than just a closing sentence. It usually includes the author's humility, gratitude, and a precise record of when the work was finished. This colophon from Nur al-Idah gives us the date Friday, 24 Jumada al-Ula, 1032 AH, and shows the author's hope that the book be accepted and beneficial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the section
Recognize that this is the khatima (conclusion) of the book. It usually contains closing prayers and the completion date.
2
Locate the completion date
Find the specific day and date mentioned, which is Friday, 24 Jumada al-Ula, 1032 AH. This is the historical record of when the author finished writing.
The date is critical for verifying the work's origin and authenticity.
3
Understand the author's prayers
The author prays for acceptance, forgiveness, and benefit. This reflects the Islamic scholarly tradition of seeking ikhlas (sincerity) and blessing on one's work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة
وهذا ما تيسر للعاجز الحقير بعناية مولاه القوي القدير.
الحمد لله الذي هدانا لهذا وما كنا لنهتدي لولا أن هدانا الله، وصلى الله على سيدنا ومولانا محمد خاتمِ رسله وأنبيائه، وعلى آله وسلَّم، وذريته ومن والاه.
وصحبه
ونسأل الله سبحانه وتعالى أن يجعله خالصاً لوجهه الكريم، وأن ينفع به النفع العميم، ويُجزِلَ به الثوابَ الجَسيم ، وأن يغفر لنا ذنوبنا، ولوالدينا ومشايخنا وإخواننا، وأن يستر عيوبنا ويرزقنا ما تَقَرُّ به عيوننا حالاً ومآلاً.
آمین
وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين، سبحان ربك رب العزة عما يصفون وسلامٌ على المرسلين، والحمد لله رب العالمين.
قال مؤلفه : انتهى تأليفه في يوم الجمعة المبارك، رابع عشرين جمادى
الأولى، سنة اثنتين وثلاثين وألف.
قال كاتبه مؤلفه حسن الشرنبلالي عفا الله عنه :
Conclusion. And this is what was facilitated for the incapable lowly one by the care of his Lord, the Strong, the All-Powerful. Praise be to Allah who guided us to this, and we would not have been guided unless Allah guided us. And may Allah send blessings upon our master and patron Muhammad, the seal of His messengers and prophets, and upon his family, and grant them peace, and upon his descendants and those who support him and his companions. And we ask Allah, the Glorified and Exalted, to make it solely for His noble face, and to benefit it with widespread benefit, and to reward us abundantly, and to forgive us our sins, and our parents, our teachers, and our brothers, and to conceal our faults and provide us with what pleases our eyes now and in the future. Ameen. And may Allah send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon his family and all his companions. Glory be to your Lord, the Lord of honor, above what they describe, and peace upon the messengers, and praise be to Allah, the Lord of the worlds. His author said: Its composition finished on the blessed Friday, the 24th of Jumada al-Ula, the year 1032. Its writer and author, Hasan al-Shurunbulali, may Allah pardon him, said:
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is the concluding section (khatima) of the book Nur al-Idah. The author, Hasan al-Shurunbulali, humbly attributes the work's completion to Allah's care. He praises Allah for guidance, sends blessings on the Prophet Muhammad, and prays that the book be accepted, beneficial, and a source of reward. He then records the exact date of completion: Friday, 24 Jumada al-Ula, 1032 AH (corresponding to 1623 CE). This colophon authenticates the work and gives it a historical context.

Key Terms
خاتمة (khatima): The conclusion of the book; contains the author's final prayers and completion date.

Understanding the Colophon of Nur al-Idah
Author's colophon and completion date

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the completion date of Nur al-Idah and explain the author's scholarly plan for the remaining acts of worship.

Core Idea
A colophon reveals the author's humility, his completion date, and his roadmap for the text.

The passage before us is not a legal ruling but the author's personal closing remarks. As you read these lines from Hasan al-Shurunbulali, you step into the workshop of a Hanafi scholar finishing his foundational work on purification and prayer, and announcing his plan to cover zakat and hajj. Understanding such front matter deepens your appreciation of the text's historical and scholarly context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's tone
Notice how al-Shurunbulali describes himself as 'the weak, humble [author]' and attributes his work to divine care. This humility is a hallmark of classical Islamic scholarship.
2
Note the completion date
The date is explicitly given: Friday, 24 Jumada al-Ula 1032 AH. This corresponds to 1623 CE. Memorizing this date links the text to its historical period.
Jumada al-Ula is the fifth month of the Islamic calendar.
3
Understand the author's intention
Al-Shurunbulali states he intends to complete the five acts of worship by adding zakat and hajj. The text already covers taharah (purification) and salah. This tells you the scope of the original Nur al-Idah and its planned continuation.
The 'five acts of worship' refer to the five pillars minus shahadah, which is covered by the book's introduction.
4
Recognize the passage type
This is a colophon (khatimah), not a legal ruling. Do not extract fiqh rules from it; appreciate it as a historical and biographical note.

Conclusion. And this is what was facilitated for the weak, humble [author] by the care of his Mighty, All-Powerful Master. Praise be to Allah who guided us to this; we would not have been guided had Allah not guided us. And may Allah bless our Master Muhammad, the Seal of His Messengers and Prophets, and his family and grant them peace, and his descendants and those who follow him. And his Companions. Its scribe/author, Hasan al-Shurunbulali, may Allah forgive him, said: Then I intended to complete the five acts of worship (1) by appending zakat and hajj in what I compiled concisely, so I said: The Book of Zakat. (1) i.e., along with taharah (purification).
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is the author's colophon, marking the conclusion of the main text of Nur al-Idah. It begins with humble gratitude and praises to Allah, followed by salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ. The author, Hasan al-Shurunbulali, states that the composition was completed on Friday, 24 Jumada al-Ula 1032 AH (corresponding to 1623 CE). In the final paragraph, he expresses his intention to complete the treatment of the five acts of worship—already including taharah (purification) and salah (prayer)—by adding concise sections on zakat and hajj. He indicates that he will begin with 'The Book of Zakat.' This colophon gives students important historical context about the work's composition and the author's scholarly plan. Note that the 'five acts of worship' refer to the five pillars: Shahadah (already covered in the book's introduction), Salah, Zakat, Sawm, and Hajj, with Taharah being a prerequisite for Salah.

Key Terms
خاتمة (khatimah): The concluding section of a book, often containing the author's remarks on completion date and future plans.

The Scholarly Apparatus: Understanding a Hanafi Fiqh Bibliography
List of references used in the study and verification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of sources listed in a Hanafi fiqh bibliography and explain their relevance to understanding the school's methodology.

Core Idea
A Hanafi fiqh book's bibliography reveals its scholarly DNA — the sources that shape its rulings.

This passage is a bibliography from a modern edition of Nur al-Idah, a foundational Hanafi text. While it may seem like a dry list, each entry is a key to understanding the chain of authority in Hanafi fiqh. By studying these sources, you learn which works the school considers authoritative and how later scholars built upon earlier ones.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the purpose
Understand that this bibliography lists the sources the editor consulted for verifying and commenting on Nur al-Idah. It is a scholarly apparatus that ensures transparency and allows readers to trace the origins of rulings.
Beware of mistaking this list for fiqh content; it is metadata about the scholarship.
2
Categorize the sources
Group the entries into categories: Hanafi mutun (e.g., Mukhtasar al-Quduri), shuruh (e.g., Maraqi al-Falah), usul works (e.g., Kanz al-Daqa'iq), hadith collections (e.g., Majma' al-Zawa'id), language references (e.g., Lisan al-'Arab), and biographical works (e.g., Lisan al-Mizan).
3
Observe the hierarchy of authority
Note that early authoritative works like al-Mabsut (by al-Sarakhsi, d. 483 AH) and Kanz al-Daqa'iq (by al-Nasafi, d. 710 AH) appear alongside later commentaries like Maraqi al-Falah (a sharh of Nur al-Idah). This reflects the layered development of Hanafi fiqh.
The presence of both original texts and commentaries helps trace the evolution of rulings.
4
Identify the role of non-fiqh sources
Sources like Lisan al-Mizan (a biographical dictionary of hadith narrators) and Fayd al-Qadir (a hadith commentary) are included because they support the verification of prophetic traditions used as evidence in fiqh.
A thorough muhaqqiq must authenticate hadith and narrators.
5
Connect to your study methodology
When you encounter a ruling in Nur al-Idah, you can use this bibliography to locate the primary sources that the author or commentator relied upon. This strengthens your ability to evaluate the strength of the proof.
This is a skill for advanced students of Hanafi fiqh.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (fihris masadir al-dirasah wa al-tahqiq) listing the scholarly sources used in the study and verification of the book. It appears at the end of the work and includes references to key Hanafi and general Islamic texts such as Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi, Kanz al-Daqa'iq by al-Nasafi, and Maraqi al-Falah Sharh Nur al-Idah. The list also includes biographical dictionaries, hadith works, and linguistic references. This section serves as an academic apparatus, documenting the authoritative sources the editor consulted. No legal rulings are contained herein; rather, it is front matter essential for understanding the scholarly foundation of the edition.

Key Terms
فهرس مصادر الدراسة والتحقيق (Fihris Masadir al-Dirasah wa al-Tahqiq): Index of study and verification sources – a bibliography listing the references used by the editor in preparing the critical edition.
المبسوط (Al-Mabsut): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work by al-Sarakhsi (d. 483 AH), considered a fundamental source in the school.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh matn by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used for memorization.
مراقي الفلاح شرح نور الإيضاح (Maraqi al-Falah Sharh Nur al-Idah): A commentary on Nur al-Idah by al-Shurunbulali (though here attributed to others? Wait – in the list it says 'Maraqi al-Falah Sharh Nur al-Idah' without author, but typically by al-Shurunbulali. In this bibliography it is under editor 'Abd al-Jalil al-'Ata. But the work is a Hanafi fiqh commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the bibliography on page 383-384, which of the following is a commentary on the text Nur al-Idah?
A) Al-Mabsut
B) Mukhtasar al-Quduri
C) Maraqi al-Falah
D) Lisan al-'Arab

Key Takeaway
A fiqh bibliography is not just a list; it maps the scholarly lineage and authority behind the rulings you study.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Hanafi Fiqh Bibliography: Key Sources in the Critical Edition of Nur al-Idah
Critical edition bibliography of Nur al-Idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi fiqh sources listed in the bibliography and explain the role of each in verifying the text of Nur al-Idah.

Core Idea
The critical edition of Nur al-Idah rests on a chain of authoritative Hanafi works, from al-Mabsut to Maraqi al-Falah.

A critical edition is only as strong as its sources. The bibliography of this edition of Nur al-Idah lists dozens of works consulted for verification. Some are core Hanafi manuals (Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Mabsut), others are commentaries (Maraqi al-Falah), and still others are hadith collections or lexicons. Understanding this bibliography helps you appreciate how later editors anchor a classical text in the broader scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Scan the bibliography format
Each entry has a number, author name, death date (Hijri), editor, publisher, and edition. Note the range: death dates span from the 2nd century (al-San'ani, d. 211) to the 9th century (al-Haythami, d. 807). This shows the depth of the critical apparatus.
The numbers restart or skip? Check the text: entries 79 to 94 are listed; some numbers are missing (e.g., 6, 81). This is a partial list from a larger index.
2
Identify the three categories of sources
Group entries by type: (a) Hanafi fiqh works: al-Mabsut (#79), Mukhtasar al-Quduri (#84), Maraqi al-Falah (#86), al-Masalik fi al-Manasik (#87); (b) Hadith works: Majma' al-Zawa'id (#81), Musannaf (#92, #93), Mustadrak (#88), Musnads (#89, #90); (c) Lexical works: Mukhtar al-Sihah (#83), al-Misbah al-Munir (#91).
al-Majmu' (#82) is a Shafi'i work – important because the editor consults even non-Hanafi fiqh for comparison.
3
Trace the relationship to Nur al-Idah
Maraqi al-Falah (#86) is the most direct: it is a detailed commentary on Nur al-Idah. Al-Mabsut (#79) by al-Sarakhsi is a foundational Hanafi reference for deriving rulings. Mukhtasar al-Quduri (#84) is a concise legal manual that Nur al-Idah itself often summarizes.
The editor uses these to check the accuracy of citations and to resolve ambiguous passages.
4
Note the editorial process
The bibliography shows that the editor relied on multiple critical editions (e.g., al-Mabsut from Dar al-Ma'rifa, Mukhtar al-Sihah from Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyya) and manuscripts (indicated by 'تحقيق' and 'إخراج'). This cross-referencing ensures textual reliability.
The presence of works like al-Mukhassas (#85) – a lexicon – shows attention to linguistic precision.

Commentary
This passage is the bibliography (فهرس المصادر) of the critical edition of Nur al-Idah. It lists the classical and contemporary works consulted for the verification and study of the text. The list includes major Hanafi fiqh references such as al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi, Maraqi al-Falah (a commentary on Nur al-Idah itself), and Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It also includes hadith collections (Musannaf, Mustadrak, Majma' al-Zawa'id) and lexical works (Mukhtar al-Sihah, al-Misbah al-Munir). The bibliography demonstrates the range of sources used in producing a reliable edition of this foundational Hanafi text.

Structure of Nur al-Idah: Table of Contents
Table of contents listing chapters of Nur al-Idah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major chapters of Nur al-Idah and explain the typical order of a Hanafi fiqh manual, starting with Taharah.

Core Idea
The table of contents reveals the systematic structure of Hanafi fiqh: beginning with purification and building step by step.

A table of contents is more than a list—it is a roadmap of the author's legal pedagogy. In classical Hanafi works, fiqh is organized logically from the essential to the derivative. This table from Nur al-Idah shows exactly that: after introductory sections, the first major chapter is Kitab al-Taharah (The Book of Purity). Understanding this structure helps you locate rulings and see how each topic relates to the others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preliminary sections
Look at the entries before 'Kitab al-Taharah'. They include the investigator's introduction, author biography, and methodology. These are not fiqh rulings but contextual material.
Classical texts often begin with such front matter.
2
Locate the first major kitab
After the front matter, the first kitab is 'Kitab al-Taharah'. This is standard in Hanafi fiqh: purification precedes all acts of worship.
Taharah is the key to salah, which is the most important pillar.
3
Trace the subheadings within Taharah
Within Taharah, the chapters flow from waters (types and rulings), to impurity removal (cisterns, wells, istinja), to toilet manners, and finally to wudu. This progression moves from the general medium of purification to the specific act.
Each subsection builds on the previous: first the water, then how to use it, then the specific purification acts.

Navigating Nur al-Idah: Structure of a Hanafi Fiqh Primer
Table of contents of Nur al-Idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the major chapters of Nur al-Idah in order and explain the logical progression of fiqh topics in a Hanafi primer.

Core Idea
The structure of a fiqh text mirrors the jurist's path from purification to prayer.

Nur al-Idah by Imam al-Shurunbulali is a concise yet comprehensive text covering the essentials of Hanafi fiqh. Its table of contents reveals the author's pedagogical sequence: starting with purification (taharah), then prayer (salat), and the details within. Understanding this structure helps you locate rulings quickly and appreciate the systematic nature of Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major chapters
Scan the Arabic headings for 'Bāb', 'Kitāb', and 'Fasl' – these mark the main divisions. List them in order as they appear.
The first chapter is 'Bāb al-Masḥ ‘alā al-Khuffayn', then 'Bāb al-Ḥayḍ wa al-Nifās', then 'Bāb al-Azjāl' (Impurities), then 'Kitāb al-Ṣalāh'.
2
Observe the topical sequence
Note that purification topics (wiping, menstruation, impurities) come before prayer. This is because taharah (purity) is a condition for the validity of prayer.
Hanafi primers typically start with taharah before moving to the pillars of Islam.
3
Recognize the subdivisions within prayers
Under 'Kitāb al-Ṣalāh', the TOC lists conditions (shurut), times (awqat), call to prayer (adhan), etc. This shows the internal logic of breaking prayer into its components.
Each sub-topic builds on the previous, e.g., conditions → times → adhan.
4
Relate the TOC to daily practice
Consider how each listed topic is relevant to a Muslim's daily worship. For example, rulings on wudu (implied in 'masḥ') and menstruation affect when and how one prays.
The TOC is a map; each chapter addresses real-life questions.

Navigating Nur al-Idah: Structure of Sujud and Jumu'ah Chapters
Table of contents for fiqh chapters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate and identify the major fiqh topics covered in the sujud and Jumu'ah sections of Nur al-Idah using the table of contents.

Core Idea
A fiqh table of contents is a roadmap: each heading signals a distinct legal topic with its own rulings.

A table of contents (fihris) is more than a list of page numbers—it reveals how the author organised the legal material. In Nur al-Idah, the chapters on sujud (prostration for forgetfulness, recitation, and gratitude) are grouped together, followed by Jumu'ah, Eidain, eclipse, and rain prayers. Understanding this structure helps you connect related rulings and anticipate the progression of topics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main sections
Look at the highest-level headings: 'باب سجود السهو' (Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness), 'باب سجود التلاوة' (Chapter of Prostration of Recitation), 'باب الجمعة' (Chapter of Friday Prayers), etc. Each 'باب' is a major chapter.
In Hanafi fiqh texts, 'باب' denotes a chapter covering a coherent set of rulings.
2
Note the subheadings within each باب
Under 'باب سجود السهو', subheadings include 'وقت القيام بسجود السهو' (Time of standing for sahw) and 'أسباب سقوط سجود السهو' (Causes for dropping sahw). These indicate detailed rulings within the chapter.
The subheadings often list the specific issues that will be addressed.
3
Observe the grouping of related topics
The first part (page 398) covers all three types of sujud (sahw, tilawah, shukr). The second part (page 399) covers prayers with community aspects (Jumu'ah, Eidain, eclipse, rain). This grouping reflects the author's pedagogical approach.
Sujud topics are about corrective actions in prayer; the later chapters are about special congregational prayers.
4
Connect page numbers to your study plan
The page numbers (e.g., 212–237) tell you where to find specific rulings. For example, 'ما يجزئ في الخطبة' is on page 230. Use this to jump directly to the needed section.
When studying, refer back to the TOC to track your progress and find cross-references.

سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): Prostration of recitation; a prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating Nur al-Idah: Structure and Sequence
Table of contents of Nur al-Idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major chapters of Nur al-Idah and explain the organizational logic behind their sequence.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah's chapter sequence reveals the Hanafi fiqh progression from communal obligations to individual acts.

A table of contents is more than a list—it is a roadmap of the author's pedagogical method. In Nur al-Idah, the chapters move from the most communal worship (Friday prayer) through Eids, special prayers, to the most personal act (funeral rites). Understanding this flow helps you grasp why rulings are grouped together and how later sections rely on earlier ones.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the book's scope
Identify that Nur al-Idah covers only acts of worship (ibadat), not transactions or family law. All chapters listed fall under 'ibadat'.
This is typical of Hanafi primers—they often split ibadat from muamalat.
2
Note the first major chapter
The book opens with Friday prayer (jum'ah), the most important weekly congregational obligation. This sets the tone for communal worship.
3
Trace the sequence: Eid, eclipse, rain, fear, funerals
Follow the order: Eid prayers (annual), eclipse prayer (occasional), rain prayer (as needed), fear prayer (exceptional), and finally funeral rulings (inevitable for everyone).
Notice the progression from fixed to variable occasions.
4
Observe the logic: from congregational to individual
The sequence moves from prayers with large congregations (Friday, Eid) to smaller groups (eclipse, rain, fear) to individual/family duties (funerals). This reflects a decreasing degree of communal obligation.
Funerals are a fard kifayah but are handled at the individual/family level.

Commentary
This is a two-page table of contents (fihris) from Nur al-Idah, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. It lists the major chapters (abwab) and their subsections. The book begins with the chapter on Friday prayer (jum'ah), covering its ruling, conditions, sermon, sunnahs, and completeness. Then follows Eid prayer, including its ruling, recommended acts, time, method, and distinctions for sacrifice. Next are eclipse prayer (kusuf), rain prayer (istisqa), and fear prayer (khawf). The final and longest section is on funerary rulings (ahkam al-jana'iz), covering the dying person, preparation, washing, shrouding, and funeral prayer. This index shows the systematic organization typical of Hanafi fiqh works, progressing from communal obligations to individual ones.

Key Terms
باب (bāb): Chapter or section heading in a fiqh book.
فهرس الموضوعات (fihris al-mawḍū'āt): Table of contents; an index of topics in the book.

Introduction and Front Matter

Navigating the Fiqh Text: Table of Contents for Vows, Itikaf, Zakat, and Sadaqah al-Fitr
Table of contents indexing multiple fiqh chapters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate specific Hanafi fiqh rulings by using the table of contents structure to identify the chapter and subheading that corresponds to a given legal topic.

Core Idea
A table of contents is a map to the fiqh text: each heading leads to detailed Hanafi rulings.

This lesson covers the table of contents from Nur al-Idah, one of the foundational texts of the Hanafi school. The table lists the chapters (kutub) and subheadings (abus) for the latter part of the book, covering vital topics like vows (al-nadhr), i'tikaf (seclusion), zakat (obligatory charity), and sadaqah al-fitr. Learning to navigate this structure efficiently will help you find the exact legal rulings you need, whether for study, fatwa, or personal practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main chapters
Scan the table of contents and note the main chapter headings: Bab al-Nadhr (Vows), Bab al-I'tikaf (Seclusion), Kitab al-Zakah (Book of Zakat), and Bab Sadaqat al-Fitr (Chapter of Fitr Charity). Each of these is a self-contained unit of Hanafi fiqh.
The word 'Bab' means chapter; 'Kitab' means book, but both serve as major divisions.
2
Read the subheadings under each chapter
Under each main heading, there are subheadings that break down the specific rulings. For example, under Bab al-Nadhr, you see 'Conditions of fulfilling a vow,' 'What is valid to vow,' etc. These guide you to the exact ruling you need.
Some subheadings are indented or listed sequentially. Note the page numbers for quick reference.
3
Trace a sample topic
Pick any subheading, such as 'Ruling on vowing to fast on the two Eids and the days of Tashreeq.' The table tells you the page where this ruling begins. In a physical book, you would turn to that page to read the detailed Hanafi position.
In digital versions, page numbers may not be exact, but the structure still guides navigation.
4
Understand the flow of the text
Notice the sequence: the table starts with vows, moves to itikaf, then zakat, and finally sadaqah al-fitr. This ordering follows the typical Hanafi fiqh arrangement (ibadat). Later sections of the book would cover muamalat and other topics.
Knowing the order helps you anticipate where a particular ruling might be found.
5
Apply to a research question
Suppose you need the Hanafi ruling on 'Enriching the poor by giving' which appears under Bab al-Masrif (Chapter of Disbursement) in the Zakat section. The table shows 'Enriching the poor by giving' as a subheading. You can now locate the exact spot in the text.
Practice by mentally searching for other subheadings like 'Trick to avoid obligation of Zakat' or 'Zakat on debt.'

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents (fihris) from the book Nur al-Idah, listing the chapters and subheadings covered in the latter part of the work. The topics include the laws of vows (al-nadhr), i'tikaf (seclusion in the mosque), zakat (obligatory charity), and sadaqah al-fitr (the charity at the end of Ramadan). The page numbers refer to the original pagination. As a Hanafi fiqh text, each heading corresponds to detailed rulings from the Hanafi school. The table of contents serves as a guide for the reader to navigate the legal discussions that follow.

Key Terms
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow; a pledge to perform an act of worship or charity that is not normally obligatory.
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Seclusion in a mosque for the purpose of worship, typically during the last ten days of Ramadan.
الزكاة (al-zakah): Obligatory charity; one of the five pillars of Islam, involving a fixed portion of wealth given to specific categories of recipients.
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan before the Eid prayer.

Key Takeaway
A table of contents is an essential navigational tool in a fiqh text; mastering its structure allows efficient access to detailed Hanafi rulings on specific topics.

Navigating the Apparatus of a Hanafi Fiqh Edition
Final pages: subject index and editor's bibliography

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of a subject index and an editor's publication list and explain their value in studying Hanafi fiqh texts.

Core Idea
The subject index and editor's works list are essential tools for accessing and evaluating the scholarly content of a Hanafi fiqh book.

When you open a critical edition of a classical Hanafi text, you often encounter front and back matter that helps you navigate the book. This lesson focuses on two such elements: the subject index (fihris al-mawdu'at) and the list of editor's published works (sadarat al-muhaqqiq). Understanding these sections will train you to use a fiqh book efficiently and appreciate the scholarly contribution of the editor.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two sections
Identify which part of the page belongs to the subject index and which belongs to the editor's list. The index is on page 408 and continues at the top of 409; the editor's list occupies the rest of 409.
The index entries are brief citations of topics with page numbers.
2
Analyze the index entries
Scan the index items: they include headings like 'Salutation upon the Prophet,' 'Visiting al-Baqi,' etc. Note that they follow the order of the book's chapters. Recognize that the index allows you to quickly find where a specific topic is discussed.
Index entries often use the same terminology as the matn (main text).
3
Examine the editor's publication list
Read through the list of works edited or authored by Dr. Saeed Bakdash. These range from monographs on Zamzam water to critical editions of Hanafi hunting manuals. Understand that this list demonstrates the editor's expertise and the scholarly context of the current edition.
The editor's other works may be referenced in footnotes or introductions.
4
Connect both sections to your study goals
Consider how you would use the subject index to find rulings on, say, 'visiting graves.' Then note how the editor's other publications could provide supplementary reading on related fiqh topics.
This skill transfers to any scholarly Hanafi work.

Commentary
This extract shows the final two pages of the edition. Page 408 contains the tail end of the subject index (fihris al-mawdu'at), covering topics such as visitation to the Prophet's grave, etiquettes of greeting, and visiting other sacred sites. It lists page numbers for chapters like 'Returning to the greeting of the Messenger of Allah' and 'Visiting al-Baqi'. Page 409 is entirely devoted to a list of works published by the editor (sadara lil-muhaqqiq), Dr. Saeed Bakdash. These are scholarly editions and studies produced by him, including books on Zamzam water, the Black Stone, hunting, and biographies of notable Hanafi scholars like Ibn Malik and Muhammad 'Abid al-Sindi al-Ansari. This front matter confirms the editor's extensive contributions to Hanafi fiqh literature and manuscript editing.

Key Terms
فهرس الموضوعات (fihris al-mawḍūʿāt): Subject index listing topics with corresponding page numbers.
صَدَرَ للمحقق (ṣadara lil-muḥaqqiq): List of works published by the editor/critical scholar.

Editor's Bibliography of Published Hanafi Works
List of books published by the researcher

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Hanafi texts published by the editor and explain their significance in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
This bibliography introduces core Hanafi texts that form the backbone of the school's relied-upon rulings.

This section is not a fiqh ruling but a list of works published by the researcher. It provides context for the edition you are studying. Understanding these texts helps you appreciate the editorial work behind the book.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and author
Read each entry and note the title, author, and death year. This establishes the source's provenance.
Authors are often referred to by their honorifics (e.g., Imam Abu al-Barakat).
2
Note its significance in the Hanafi school
Pay attention to phrases like 'one of the most important relied-upon texts' or 'author mentions only the saying of the Imam.' This indicates the work's authority level.
Texts that only transmit Abu Hanifa's view are often given higher weight in fatwa.
3
Recognize editorial details
Observe the number of manuscript copies used and the edition number. This reflects the critical effort to produce a reliable text.
More manuscripts generally mean a more thorough edition.

٢٤ ـ المختار للفتوى، في مذهب الإمام الأعظم أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه، للإمام عبد الله بن محمود الموصلي، (ت٦٨٣هـ) ، أحد أهم المتون المعتمدة في المذهب، تم تحقيقه بالاعتماد على ۱۷ نسخة خطية، في مجلد مشرق، في (٥٦٠) صفحة، ولا يَذكرُ فيه مؤلفه إلا قول الإمام، مع دراسة عنه، وعن منهجه، وبيان شروحه البالغة (۱۷) شرحاً، ط/١ (١٤٣٣هـ).
٢٥ ـ نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح، للإمام الشرنبلالي حسن بن عمار، (ت ١٠٦٩هـ)، مختصر مهم معتمد مشهور عند متأخري الحنفية، يضم الأحكام الفقهية المتعلقة بالعبادات فقط إلى آخر الحج دون بقية الأبواب، تم تحقيقه على ١٣ نسخة خطية، في مجلد مُشرِق ، يقع في (٤١٦) صفحة، ط/١ (١٤٣٣هـ).
٢٦ ـ زاد الفقير ، مختصر نادر لطيف خاص بأحكام الصلاة فقط على مذهب السادة الحنفية، فيه مسائلُ كثيرةٌ مهمةٌ يَعِزُّ الوقوف عليها في غيره، للإمام الكمال ابن الهمام، (ت٨٦١هـ)، صاحب: «فتح القدير» شرح الهداية، تم تحقيقه على عشر نسخ خطية، مع ترجمة موسعة لابن الهمام، وفيها بيان بلوغه رتبة الاجتهاد،
صَدَرَ للمحقق
٤١٣
وذكر ما وقفت عليه من ترجيحاته الفقهية والمسائل التي خالف فيها مذهبه الحنفي، وكذلك ذكر اختياراته في الأصول وقواعد الاستنباط التي خالف فيها أصول الحنفية، وقد جاء مطبوعاً في مجلد مشرق، يقع في (٢٠٨) صفحة،
١٤٣٤/١هـ.
۲۷ - أصولُ البَزْدَوِيُّ (كنز الوصول إلى معرفة الأصول)، للإمام فخر الإسلام أبي العسر علي بن محمد البَزْدَوِي الحنفي ، (ت٤٨٢هـ)، من أعظم كتب الإسلام في علم أصول الفقه على المذهب الحنفي، يمتاز بسردِه الأدلة على قواعد استنباط الأحكام، مع تطبيقات لها على فروع فقهية كثيرة، وقد حقق على عَشْرِ نُسَخ خطية
نفيسة نادرة.
وطبع معه: تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي، للإمام قاسم بن قطلوبغا الحنفي، (ت٨٧٩هـ)، مع ربط تخريج كل حديث في موضعه، وتمَّ جَمْعُ شَمْلِ الكتابين معاً في مجلد واحد مُشرِق ، في ٨٣٢ صفحة، ط١٤٣٦/١هـ.
۲۸ - تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي، للإمام العلامة قاسم بن قُطلُوبُغا، (ت٨٧٩هـ)، وهو كتاب نفيس من كتب تخريج الأحاديث والآثار، ولم يُخْلِه مؤلّفه من استدراكات دقيقة على البزدوي مع إمامته، وإفادات أصولية واستدلالية بثها في ثناياه، وقد حقق على نسخة بخط المؤلّف، وأخرى عليها خطه وإجازته به لتلميذه، مطبوع مع
أصول البزدوي، في مجلدٍ واحدٍ مُشرِق ، في ٨۳۲ صفحة، ط١٤٣٦/١هـ. ٢٩ ـ الجوهرة النيرة شرح مختصر القدوري (ت (٤٢٨هـ)، للإمام أبي بكر بن علي الحداد، من زبيد اليمن، (ت٨٠٠هـ)، كتاب مبارك رفيع نفيس، ساطع نوره، متألق في حسنه، لم يسمح الدهرُ بمثاله، ولم ينسج ناسج على منواله، سهل العبارة، قريب المعنى، يحتاجه المبتدي والمرتوي من الحنفية ،وغيرهم، مليء بالمسائل الفقهية وفروعها، مع ذكره للأدلة، وبيان وجه الدلالة بما يطرب له طالب العلم، هذا مع ذكره لخلاف الفقهاء، وبيان وجهة نظر كل منهم باختصار ، وقد تم تحقيقه على أربع عشر نسخة خطية، مع تخريج أحاديثه، والعناية بتفقير مسائله وفروعه، وتم وضع مختصر
القدوري بأعلى صفحاته، وقد جاء في ست مجلدات، ط١٤٣٦/١هـ.

Commentary
This passage is a front matter list of books published by the researcher/editor (Dr. Saeed Bakdash). It is not part of the original fiqh text of Nur al-Idah. The list includes descriptions of major Hanafi works such as Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Mukhtar lil-Fatwa, Nur al-Idah, Zad al-Faqir, Usul al-Bazdawi, al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah, and others. Each entry provides the author, death date, significance, editorial methodology (number of manuscripts used, physical description), and edition details. This bibliography serves as an introduction to the editor's scholarly contributions and the texts he has researched. Students should recognize this as paratextual material that does not convey fiqh rulings but rather situates the edition within a broader publishing project.

Key Terms
صَدَرَ للمحقق (ṣadara li-l-muḥaqqiq): Published by the researcher/editor — a heading indicating that the following list enumerates books that have been published or edited by the same person.
ط/١ (ṭ/1): First edition (of the edited work).
نسخ خطية (nusakh khaṭṭiyyah): Manuscript copies used for the critical edition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Canon of Hanafi Scholarly Editions: Four Landmark Works
Editorial preface listing four published Hanafi scholarly works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify four major Hanafi texts and explain their roles in the Hanafi curriculum and their interrelationships.

Core Idea
A scholar’s edition is not just a reprint—it is a critical reconstruction of authoritative Hanafi texts.

This passage from the editor’s preface lists four scholarly works he has published. Although it appears as front matter, it is a valuable window into the backbone of Hanafi learning: the usul text of al-Bazdawi, the takhrij of its hadiths, the commentary al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah on the classic matn Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and the matn Bidayat al-Mubtadi that underlies the great commentary al-Hidayah. Understanding these works and their relationships is essential for any student of Hanafi fiqh and usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify each work’s genre and author
List the four works: Usul al-Bazdawi (usul al-fiqh), Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi (hadith authenticator), al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah (sharh of Mukhtasar al-Quduri), and Bidayat al-Mubtadi (matn for al-Hidayah). For each, note the author and century.
The works span the 5th to 8th centuries AH, showing the continuity of Hanafi scholarship.
2
Understand the relationship between matn and sharh
Note that al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is a commentary (sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and Bidayat al-Mubtadi is itself a matn that was later commented upon by its own author al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah. This layered structure is typical of Hanafi learning.
A matn is a concise text; a sharh expands it. The same author may write both.
3
Recognize the importance of takhrij in usul
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha’s Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi verifies the hadiths cited by al-Bazdawi. This shows how usul al-fiqh relies on authenticated prophetic evidence.
Takhrij is a critical discipline that strengthens the evidentiary foundation of legal theory.
4
Appreciate editorial methodology
The editor mentions the number of manuscripts used (10, 14, 8) and the layout (placing the matn at the top of the page). This reflects the scholarly rigor required to produce a reliable edition.
Knowing the editorial base helps assess the authority of the published text.

Published by the editor. He mentioned what I found of his juristic preferences and issues in which he opposed his Hanafi school, as well as his choices in principles and rules of deduction in which he opposed Hanafi principles. It has been printed in a luminous volume, in 208 pages, 1434 AH. 27 - Usul al-Bazdawi (Kan al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul), by Imam Fakhr al-Islam Abi al-Usr 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi al-Hanafi (d. 482 AH), one of the greatest books of Islam in the science of Usul al-Fiqh according to the Hanafi school. It is distinguished by its presentation of evidence for the rules of deriving rulings, with applications to many juristic branches. It was critically edited based on ten rare precious manuscripts. And with it is printed: Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi, by Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi (d. 879 AH), with linking the source of each hadith in its place. It is a precious book among the books of takhrij of hadiths and athar. Its author did not leave it without precise objections against al-Bazdawi despite his imamate, and usul-related and evidential benefits he scattered within it. It was edited from a copy in the author's handwriting and another with his handwriting and his authorization to his student. Printed with Usul al-Bazdawi in one luminous volume, 832 pages, 1st edition 1436 AH. 29 - Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), by Imam Abu Bakr ibn 'Ali al-Haddad, from Zabid, Yemen (d. 800 AH). A blessed, elevated, precious book, radiant in its beauty, brilliant in its perfection. Time has not allowed its like, and no weaver has woven upon its pattern. Easy in expression, close in meaning, needed by both the beginner and the advanced among the Hanafis and others. Full of juristic issues and their branches, with mention of evidence, and explanation of the aspect of indication in a way that delights the student of knowledge. This in addition to mentioning the differences among jurists and briefly explaining each one's perspective. It was edited based on fourteen manuscripts, with takhrij of its hadiths, and attention to paragraphing its issues and branches. Mukhtasar al-Quduri was placed at the top of its pages. It came in six volumes, 1st edition 1436 AH. Published by the editor. 30 - Bidayat al-Mubtadi, by Imam 'Ali ibn Abi Bakr al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH). It is among the most important reliable texts in Hanafi fiqh due to its strong connection with the most famous books of the Hanafis and the most prevalent among them. It is the book 'al-Hidayah' by al-Marghinani himself, for 'al-Hidayah' is a commentary on the abridgment: 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', and al-Hidayah is an abridged commentary of his comprehensive great commentary on it: 'Kifayat al-Muntahi', consisting of eighty volumes. The author collected in 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' between 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' (d. 428 AH) and 'al-Jami' al-Saghir' by Imam Muhammad (d. 189 AH), with additions. Allah facilitated its editing and service based on eight precious manuscripts. It was revived after an old corrupted and altered edition, with attention to paragraphing its issues, resolving its difficult points, and commenting on it with necessary matters about the book and its author and stating his methodology in it. It came in one luminous volume, 728 pages, 1st edition 1436 AH, along with a study.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a list of four published scholarly works, presented by the editor of the present volume (Nur al-Idah). It serves as a front matter advertisement of the editor's other critical editions. The passage begins by mentioning a prior work (apparently a book on the editor's own juristic preferences and methodological choices) and then proceeds to describe four major Hanafi texts that the editor has published: (1) Usul al-Bazdawi, a foundational work in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, edited from ten manuscripts, and paired with Qutlubugha's takhrij of its hadiths; (2) the separate takhrij work by Qutlubugha, which includes critical remarks on al-Bazdawi's text; (3) Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, a commentary by al-Haddad on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a key Hanafi fiqh text, edited from fourteen manuscripts and printed with the matn at the top; and (4) Bidayat al-Mubtadi by al-Marghinani, the base text for his famous commentary al-Hidayah, edited from eight manuscripts. For each, the editor highlights the significance of the work, its relation to other Hanafi classics, and the editorial methodology (number of manuscripts used, layout features). The passage functions as a scholarly bibliography demonstrating the editor's contributions to Hanafi textual scholarship.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): A classical Hanafi work on usul al-fiqh by Imam al-Bazdawi, considered one of the greatest works in the field, presenting evidence for legal derivation rules with applications.
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah): A commentary by al-Haddad on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh matn, known for its clear exposition, inclusion of evidence, and mention of juristic differences.
بداية المبتدي (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): A Hanafi fiqh text by al-Marghinani, combining Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir with additions; it is the base text for al-Marghinani's own commentary al-Hidayah.

D) Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Key Takeaway
The editor's preface illustrates the interrelationship of key Hanafi texts and the critical scholarship needed to preserve them.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Understanding Bidayat al-Mubtadi: The Foundation of Hanafi Fiqh Study
Describing the significance and lineage of an essential Hanafi matn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the lineage of Bidayat al-Mubtadi and explain its relationship to Al-Hidayah and Kifayat al-Muntahi.

Core Idea
Bidayat al-Mubtadi is the matn that al-Marghinani later commented on as Al-Hidayah — the central Hanafi reference.

This lesson introduces you to one of the most important foundational texts in the Hanafi madhhab. The passage describes how Imam al-Marghinani compiled Bidayat al-Mubtadi by merging two earlier authoritative works. Understanding this text's lineage is crucial for any student of Hanafi fiqh, because it is the base upon which the great commentary Al-Hidayah is built.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and title
Note the full title 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' and its author, Imam Ali ibn Abi Bakr al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH).
Al-Marghinani is the same author of Al-Hidayah.
2
Understand the contents
The matn combines two sources: Mukhtasar al-Quduri (by al-Quduri) and Al-Jami' al-Saghir (by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), with additions.
It is not an original work but a compilation of two authoritative texts.
3
Trace the commentary lineage
Al-Marghinani wrote a massive commentary Kifayat al-Muntahi (80 volumes), then abridged it into Al-Hidayah, which is the commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi.
Al-Hidayah is thus an abridged commentary on his own matn.
4
Recognize its importance
Because Al-Hidayah became the central reference for Hanafi fiqh worldwide, its matn (Bidayat al-Mubtadi) is equally foundational.
Many later commentaries and glosses are based on Al-Hidayah.

Published by the researcher: 30 - Bidayat al-Mubtadi, by Imam Ali ibn Abi Bakr al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), one of the most important relied-upon texts in Hanafi fiqh; due to its close connection with the most famous and widely circulated books of the Hanafis, which is the book 'Al-Hidayah' by al-Marghinani himself, for 'Al-Hidayah' is a commentary on the abridgment: 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', and Al-Hidayah is an abridged commentary from his extensive great commentary: 'Kifayat al-Muntahi', which runs to eighty volumes. Allah facilitated its verification and service from eight precious manuscript copies, and it was revived after an old distorted and altered edition, with attention to parsing its issues, correcting its difficulties, and providing necessary commentary on the book and its author, and explaining his methodology in it. Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is an editorial introduction describing the book 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' by Imam al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH). It highlights the book's central importance in the Hanafi madhhab due to its direct connection to 'Al-Hidayah', which is al-Marghinani's own commentary on this matn. The author compiled it by merging two earlier authoritative works: 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) and 'Al-Jami' al-Saghir' by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH), adding supplementary material. The passage also notes that 'Al-Hidayah' itself is an abridgment of al-Marghinani's larger commentary 'Kifayat al-Muntahi', an eighty-volume work. The editorial work involved comparing eight manuscripts to produce a corrected edition, replacing a previous corrupted print.

Key Terms
بداية المبتدي (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): A foundational Hanafi fiqh matn by al-Marghinani combining Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir with additions.
الهداية (Al-Hidayah): Al-Marghinani's commentary on his own matn Bidayat al-Mubtadi, which became a central reference in Hanafi fiqh.
كفاية المنتهي (Kifayat al-Muntahi): Al-Marghinani's extensive original commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, running to eighty volumes, from which Al-Hidayah was abridged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between Bidayat al-Mubtadi and Al-Hidayah?
A) Al-Hidayah is a commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi.
B) Bidayat al-Mubtadi is a commentary on Al-Hidayah.
C) They are independent works by different authors.
D) Al-Hidayah is a summary of Bidayat al-Mubtadi.

Key Takeaway
Bidayat al-Mubtadi is the matn upon which Al-Hidayah, the most widely studied Hanafi commentary, is based; it itself is a compilation of Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
